الواجب في حق الرسل عليهم السلام
- الصدق (۳) في دعواهم للرسالة وفيما يبلغونه عن الله تعالى، وحقيقة الصدق مطابقة الخبر لما في نفس الأمر وافق الاعتقاد أو لا.
(٤)
- الأمانة : وهي حفظ جوارحهم الظاهرة والباطنة من الوقوع في محرّم أو مكروه (4) .
(0)
- تبليغ ما أمروا بتبليغه للخلق )
- الفطانة والذكاء.
(۱) خصوصاً في الأسرار الإلهية والأمور الأخروية.(س).
(۲) المراد بالوجوب هنا عدم الانفكاك ولو بالدليل الشرعي، لأن وجوب الأمانة والتبليغ بدليل شرعي وأما وجوب الصدق فبدليل عقلي على أن دلالة المعجزة عقلية، أو وضعي بناء على أن دلالتها وضعية لأنها منزلة منزلة قوله تعالى صدق عبدي فيما يقول، ودلالته وضعية وهذا ظاهر كلام السنوسي ، والصحيح أنه عادي بناء على أن دلالتها عادية، أي مستندة للعادة الجارية بأن تلك معجزة علامة على الصدق (ج) بتصرف يسير (۳) اعلم أن الصدق ثلاثة أقسام : الصدق في دعوى الرسالة والصدق في الأحكام التي يبلغونها عن الله تعالى، والصدق في الكلام المتعلق بأمور الدنيا كقام زيد وقعد عمرو وأكلت كذا أو شربت كذا ونحو ذلك، والمراد هنا القسمان الأولان ، لأن البرهان المذكور فيما يأتي إنما يدل عليهما، وأما القسم الثالث فهو داخل في الأمانة. فإن قيل كل من القسمين الأولين داخل أيضاً في الأمانة بل التبليغ أيضاً داخل فيها فلا وجه فيه لإفراد ذلك عنها ، أجيب بأنه قد تقدم أن خطر الجهل في هذا الفن عظيم فلا يكتفى فيه بالإجمال(ج) بتصرف يسير. (٤) وعرفها بعضهم بعدم خيانتهم بفعل محرّم أو مكروه، وقال بعضهم هي ملكة راسخة في النفس تمنع صاحبها من ارتكاب المنهيات وعلى كل فهي ترجع إلى العصمة التي عبر بها بعضهم (ج) بتصرف يسير. (٥) الأقسام ثلاثة الأول ما أمروا بتبليغه والثاني ما أمروا بكتمانه، والثالث ما خيروا فيه فالأول هو الواجب عليهم أن يبلغوه ويجب علينا الاعتقاد بأنهم قد بلغوه ، والثاني يجب عليهم كتمانه، ويجب علينا الاعتقاد بأنهم قد كتموه والثالث خيروا فيه فيخبرون به من شاؤوا.(س).
The obligatory (attributes) regarding the messengers, peace be upon them: - Truthfulness in their claim to messengership and in what they convey from Allah Almighty. The reality of truthfulness is the correspondence of the report with what is in actual fact, whether it agrees with belief or not. - Trustworthiness: and it is the preservation of their external and internal faculties from falling into what is forbidden or disliked. - Conveyance of what they are commanded to convey to creation. - Intelligence and acumen. (1) Especially regarding divine secrets and matters of the Hereafter. (S). (2) What is meant by obligation here is non-detachment, even by a legal proof, because the obligation of trustworthiness and conveyance is by legal proof, whereas the obligation of truthfulness is by a rational proof, based on the fact that the indication of the miracle is rational, or conventional based on the fact that its indication is conventional because it is treated like the saying of Allah Almighty 'My servant has spoken truthfully in what he says', and its indication is conventional; this is apparent from the statement of al-Sanusi. The correct view is that it is customary, based on the fact that its indication is customary, i.e., based on the ongoing custom that such a miracle is a sign of truthfulness. (J) with slight modification. (3) Know that truthfulness is of three divisions: truthfulness in the claim of messengership, truthfulness in the rulings they convey from Allah Almighty, and truthfulness in speech concerning worldly matters such as 'Zayd stood', 'Amr sat', 'I ate such-and-such' or 'I drank such-and-such', and so forth. What is meant here are the first two divisions, because the proof mentioned later only indicates them. As for the third division, it is included within trustworthiness. If it is said that each of the first two divisions is also included within trustworthiness, indeed even conveyance is also included within it, so there is no point in separating them from it, the answer is that it has been mentioned earlier that the danger of ignorance in this art is great, so one is not satisfied with generality. (J) with slight modification. (4) Some defined it as their not betraying by doing something forbidden or disliked. Some said it is a firmly rooted faculty in the soul that prevents its possessor from committing prohibited acts. In any case, it reduces to infallibility ('isma), which some have expressed. (J) with slight modification. (5) The divisions are three: the first is what they were commanded to convey; the second is what they were commanded to conceal; and the third is what they were given a choice about. The first is that which is obligatory upon them to convey, and it is obligatory upon us to believe that they have conveyed it. The second is that which is obligatory upon them to conceal, and it is obligatory upon us to believe that they have concealed it. The third is that which they were given a choice about; they inform about it whomever they wish. (S).
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains the four obligatory attributes of messengers (rusul). It is a classification with definitions.

1. **Truthfulness (al-ṣidq)**: This applies to their claim of messengership and to what they convey from Allah. The definition of truthfulness is correspondence between the report and reality, regardless of whether the speaker's belief matches the report. The author then notes that truthfulness is divided into three types: (a) truthfulness in the claim of messengership, (b) truthfulness in the rulings conveyed from Allah, and (c) truthfulness in everyday speech. Only the first two are meant here, as the proof (of miracles) demonstrates them. The third type falls under trustworthiness. An objection is raised: if the first two are also included in trustworthiness, why separate them? The answer: the serious danger of ignorance in this field demands explicit enumeration.

2. **Trustworthiness (al-amāna)**: It is the preservation of one's external and internal faculties from falling into forbidden or disliked actions. Alternate definitions are given: refraining from betraying by committing forbidden or disliked acts, or a deeply-rooted quality preventing sins. Ultimately, it reduces to infallibility ('iṣma).

3. **Conveyance (al-tablīgh)**: They must convey what they are commanded to convey. The division of what is revealed into three categories (commanded to convey, commanded to conceal, given choice) is elaborated. For the first category, it is obligatory for them to convey and for us to believe they did. For the second, it is obligatory for them to conceal and for us to believe they did. For the third, they have the option.

4. **Intelligence and acumen (al-fiṭāna wa al-dhakā')**: This is mentioned briefly.

The passage also discusses the basis of obligation: truthfulness is known rationally (or conventionally/customarily, depending on the view), while trustworthiness and conveyance are known from legal proof. The note highlights that the obligation here means that these attributes are inseparable from messengers, even if proof for them comes from different sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that truthfulness in everyday speech is proven by the miracle of prophethood.
Correction: The author clarifies that only truthfulness in the claim of messengership and in religious rulings is proven by miracles. Truthfulness in worldly speech falls under trustworthiness, not the specific proof.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, into how many divisions is truthfulness (al-ṣidq) divided?
A) Two: in claim and in religious rulings.
B) Three: in claim, in religious rulings, and in worldly speech.
C) Four: in claim, in conveyance, in trustworthiness, and in character.
D) One: only in what they convey from Allah.

Key Takeaway
The four obligatory attributes of messengers are truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveyance, and intelligence; they ensure the integrity and reliability of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in the messengers, but are you truthful in your own claim? The messengers' truthfulness was proven by miracles. What miracle in your life testifies to the truthfulness of your faith? If none, what will you do today to make your faith correspond to reality?
?
The messengers preserved their faculties from the forbidden. Which of your faculties—your tongue, your eyes, your hands—do you most often use in disobedience? What one concrete step will you take this week to guard that faculty as the messengers guarded theirs?
?
You have been commanded to convey what you know of the religion, but are you selective in what you share out of fear or convenience? Which truth about Islam have you been hiding or softening? Write it down and commit to sharing it with someone this week, even if it costs you comfort.

The Four Obligatory Attributes of Prophets
Lists the four obligatory attributes of prophets and explains the concept of obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four attributes that are obligatory for prophets and the meaning of 'obligatory' in this context.

Core Idea
Prophets must possess truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivery, and intelligence.

This lesson introduces the four essential attributes that every prophet must have. These attributes are derived from rational and legal proofs, and they form the foundation of prophetic credibility. The passage also explains the concept of obligation, which here means that these qualities are inseparable from the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview of the four attributes. Notice how each is introduced and briefly defined.
The passage uses numbers and annotations; don't get distracted by them.
2
Identify the four attributes
List the four attributes: truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivery, and intelligence. Note the short definitions given for each.
3
Understand the meaning of obligation
The passage explains that 'obligatory' here means non-detachment — these attributes cannot be absent from a Prophet, even if proven by legal or rational evidence.
The proof for truthfulness is rational via miracles; for trustworthiness and delivery it is legal.
4
Reflect on the proofs
Consider why truthfulness is proven rationally while the other two are proven legally. This connects to the role of miracles in confirming prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواجب في حق الرسل عليهم السلام - الصدق (۳) في دعواهم للرسالة وفيما يبلغونه عن الله تعالى، وحقيقة الصدق مطابقة الخبر لما في نفس الأمر وافق الاعتقاد أو لا. (٤) - الأمانة : وهي حفظ جوارحهم الظاهرة والباطنة من الوقوع في محرّم أو مكروه (4) . (0) - تبليغ ما أمروا بتبليغه للخلق ) - الفطانة والذكاء. (۱) خصوصاً في الأسرار الإلهية والأمور الأخروية.(س). (۲) المراد بالوجوب هنا عدم الانفكاك ولو بالدليل الشرعي، لأن وجوب الأمانة والتبليغ بدليل شرعي وأما وجوب الصدق فبدليل عقلي على أن دلالة المعجزة عقلية، أو وضعي بناء على أن دلالتها وضعية لأنها منزلة منزلة قوله تعالى صدق عبدي فيما يقول، ودلالته وضعية وهذا ظاهر كلام السنوسي ، والصحيح أنه عادي بناء على أن دلالتها عادية، أي مستندة للعادة الجارية بأن تلك معجزة علامة على الصدق (ج) بتصرف يسير (۳) اعلم أن الصدق ثلاثة أقسام : الصدق في دعوى الرسالة والصدق في الأحكام التي يبلغونها عن الله تعالى، والصدق في الكلام المتعلق بأمور الدنيا كقام زيد وقعد عمرو وأكلت كذا أو شربت كذا ونحو ذلك، والمراد هنا القسمان الأولان ، لأن البرهان المذكور فيما يأتي إنما يدل عليهما، وأما القسم الثالث فهو داخل في الأمانة. فإن قيل كل من القسمين الأولين داخل أيضاً في الأمانة بل التبليغ أيضاً داخلاً فيها فلا وجه لإفراد ذلك عنها ، أجيب بأنه قد تقدم أن خطر الجهل في هذا الفن عظيم فلا يكتفى فيه بالإجمال(ج) بتصرف يسير. (٤) وعرفها بعضهم بعدم خيانتهم بفعل محرّم أو مكروه، وقال بعضهم هي ملكة راسخة في النفس تمنع صاحبها من ارتكاب المنهيات وعلى كل فهي ترجع إلى العصمة التي عبر بها بعضهم (ج) بتصرف يسير. (٥) الأقسام ثلاثة الأول ما أمروا بتبليغه والثاني ما أمروا بكتمانه، والثالث ما خيروا فيه فالأول هو الواجب عليهم أن يبلغوه ويجب علينا الاعتقاد بأنهم قد بلغوه ، والثاني يجب عليهم كتمانه، ويجب علينا الاعتقاد بأنهم قد كتموه والثالث خيروا فيه فيخبرون به من شاؤوا.(س).
The obligatory in the right of the messengers, peace be upon them: - Truthfulness in their claim to messengership and in what they convey from Allah, and the reality of truthfulness is the correspondence of the report to what is in actual fact, whether it matches belief or not. - Trustworthiness: it is the preservation of their external and internal limbs from falling into what is forbidden or disliked. - Delivery of what they are commanded to deliver to creation. - Intelligence and quickness of understanding. (1) Especially in divine secrets and matters of the afterlife. (2) The meaning of obligation here is non-detachment even by a legal proof, because the obligation of trustworthiness and delivery is by a legal proof, while the obligation of truthfulness is by a rational proof. ... (3) Know that truthfulness is of three types: truthfulness in claiming messengership, truthfulness in the rulings they convey from Allah, and truthfulness in speech concerning worldly matters. What is meant here are the first two types, because the proof mentioned later only indicates them. As for the third type, it is included in trustworthiness. ... (4) Some defined it as their not betraying by committing a forbidden or disliked act. And some said it is a deeply rooted quality in the soul that prevents its possessor from committing prohibitions. ... (5) The types are three: the first is what they are commanded to deliver, the second is what they are commanded to conceal, and the third is what they are given a choice in. The first is obligatory for them to deliver, and we must believe that they have delivered it. The second is obligatory for them to conceal, and we must believe that they have concealed it. The third they have a choice in, so they inform whomever they wish.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage defines and discusses the four obligatory attributes of prophets: truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivery, and intelligence. It begins by listing them. Then it provides a detailed commentary: on truthfulness, it explains that it is correspondence with reality. On trustworthiness, it explains it as preservation from sin. On delivery, it notes that not everything the prophet knows must be delivered; there are three categories: obligatory delivery, obligatory concealment, and optional. The passage also discusses the proof for truthfulness being rational (via miracles) versus legal, and the rationale for separating truthfulness from trustworthiness despite overlap.

Key Terms
الصدق
الأمانة
التبليغ
الفطانة
الوجوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'obligatory' means the attribute is required but can be absent occasionally.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'obligatory' here means non-detachment — the attribute must always be present and never absent from a prophet.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does 'obligatory' (الوجوب) mean in the context of prophetic attributes?
A) It is a recommended quality
B) It means the attribute is never absent from a prophet
C) It means the attribute is proven only by legal evidence
D) It means the attribute is shared with ordinary humans

Key Takeaway
The four attributes are essential for prophets and are proven by rational and legal evidence, with obligation meaning they are inseparable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If truthfulness means every report from a prophet corresponds to reality, what does that demand of your attitude toward every word of the Quran and Sunnah? Do you treat any part of it as less than absolute truth in your daily decisions?
?
The lesson defines trustworthiness as preservation from forbidden actions—outward and inward. Which inward forbidden action (e.g., pride, envy, showing off) do you most struggle to preserve yourself from, and what one step will you take today to guard against it?
?
Delivery is obligatory for prophets—they conveyed what they were commanded. You are not a prophet, but you know truths from this lesson that others do not. Whom will you share this with, and by when will you do it?

The Three Types of Truthfulness
Defines the three types of truthfulness and addresses an objection about overlapping with trustworthiness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of prophetic truthfulness and why worldly truthfulness is included under trustworthiness.

Core Idea
Truthfulness in claiming prophethood and in conveying divine rulings is distinct from everyday truthfulness.

This lesson delves into the attribute of truthfulness. The author explains that truthfulness has three types, but only two are uniquely prophetic; the third is encompassed by trustworthiness. The passage also addresses an objection about redundancy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on truthfulness types
Read the Arabic passage that discusses the three divisions of truthfulness. Identify what each type refers to.
The passage mentions three types: in claiming prophethood, in conveying rulings, and in worldly matters.
2
Understand why only two types are meant
The author states that only the first two types are relevant for the proof of prophethood; the third is included under trustworthiness.
3
Analyze the objection and answer
An objection is raised: why separate truthfulness from trustworthiness if the first two types also fall under trustworthiness? The answer is that the subject is too important to be left vague.
The answer emphasizes that the gravity of the field requires explicit mention.
4
Reflect on the pedagogical wisdom
Consider why the author insists on listing truthfulness separately despite overlap. This highlights the care needed in theological matters.

?

?

?

Are you confident in the rational basis of your faith, or do you lean on emotion? This lesson calls you to understand the logic behind prophethood. How will you strengthen your reasoned convictions?

Trustworthiness and the Three Categories of Delivery
Defines trustworthiness and enumerates the three categories of what prophets must deliver, conceal, or may choose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of prophetic trustworthiness and the three categories of what prophets must deliver, conceal, or may choose.

Core Idea
Prophets are trustworthy in all acts, and their delivery of revelation is categorized into obligatory, prohibited, and optional.

This lesson covers the attribute of trustworthiness and the related duty of delivery. The author explains that trustworthiness is a quality that prevents sin, and that not everything prophets know must be shared; there are specific categories of what must be delivered, what must be concealed, and what is optional.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on trustworthiness
Read the Arabic definitions of trustworthiness. Note the different definitions given by scholars.
One definition focuses on not committing sin; another defines it as a ingrained quality that prevents sin.
2
Understand the three categories of delivery
Identify the three categories: obligatory delivery, obligatory concealment, and optional. Understand the corresponding obligations for believers.
For each category, the passage states the prophet's duty and our required belief.
3
Relate trustworthiness to delivery
Reflect on how delivery is an aspect of trustworthiness: prophets are entrusted with messages and must convey them faithfully.
4
Consider the legal proof
Remember from Lesson 1 that trustworthiness and delivery are proven by legal evidence (samʿī). This shows their basis in revelation.

?

?
When given a choice in matters of faith (like optional acts), do you choose to share them with others or keep them to yourself? What does your choice reveal about your trustworthiness?

The Impossible Attributes of Prophets: Lying and Treachery
Sanusi defines the impossible attributes of prophets: lying and treachery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the impossible attributes of prophets are and the precise definitions of lying and treachery in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Lying and treachery are rationally impossible for prophets, defined by their essence.

Sanusi begins by enumerating the attributes that are impossible for prophets, which are the opposites of their obligatory attributes. He defines lying and treachery with precision, showing that these qualities cannot be attributed to the messengers of Allah. This passage establishes the foundation for prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the definitions of lying and treachery. Note that lying is defined by non-correspondence, not by intention.
Lying is about factual mismatch, not belief.
2
Understand the nuance on disliked actions
Notice that the passage distinguishes between disliked actions done for legislation (which are permissible for prophets) and actual disliked actions (which are impossible).
This nuance protects the principle of infallibility.
3
Connect to obligatory attributes
Recall that truthfulness and trustworthiness are obligatory for prophets; thus their opposites are impossible.

المستحيل في حق الرسل عليهم السلام يستحيل في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام أضداد الصفات الواجبة وهي كما يلي : - الكذب وحقيقة الكذب عدم مطابقة الخبر لما في نفس الأمر سواء وافق الاعتقاد أم لا. - الخيانة : بفعل شيء مما نهوا عنه نهي تحريم كالزنا وشرب الخمر، أو كراهة كقراءة القرآن في الركوع والسجود مثلاً. وأما وقوع المكروه منهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام في بعض الأوقات للتشريع فجائز، وإنما المكروه المستحيل عليهم هو الذي لم يقع بقصد التشريع فإنه لا يقع منهم. فالأمانة واجبة لهم والخيانة مستحيلة عليهم، فهم معصومون من الصغائر والكبائر قبل النبوة وبعدها فلا يقع منهم محرّم ولا مكروه لا عمداً ولا سهواً من حين فطرتهم إلى حين انتقالهم إلى دار الكرامة. ملاحظة : جاء في الحديث كل خلة يطبع عليها المؤمن إلا الخيانة والكذب (۳) (1) المراد بالكراهة هنا ما يشمل خلاف الأولى ولا يرد على ذلك أنه بال قائماً وتوضأ مرة مرة وتوضأ مرتين مرتين لأنه بال للتشريع ولبيان الجواز ، وذلك واجب في حقه الهلال لو فعلم مما تقرر أنه لا يقع منهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام محرم ولا مكروه على وجه كونه مكروهاً وكذا لا يقع منهم مباح على وجه كونه مباحاً بل على وجه كونه قربة أو للتشريع أو للتقوي على العبادات أو نحو ذلك، فأفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب فقط ، كيف وقد يتفق ذلك لبعض أوليائه فبالأولى أن يكون لصفوة الله من خلقه .(ج). (۲) واعلم أنه لا فرق بين الصغيرة والكبيرة فلا تقع منهم صغيرة ولا كبيرة ولو سهواً قبل البعثة وبعدها، لا يقال ما كان سهواً أو قبل البعثة ليس بمعصية، لأنا نقول هو صورة المعصية، وما ورد مما يوهم وقوع ذلك منهم يجب تأويله. (ج). تأويله.(ج). (۳) رواه القضاعي في مسند الشهاب عن مصعب بن سعد عن أبيه قال : رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : " يطبع المؤمن على كل خلة خلا الخيانة والكذب . ورواه ابن أبي الدنيا في مكارم الأخلاق عن مصعب بن سعد عن أبيه قال رسول الله له على كل خلة يطبع أو يطوى المؤمن إلا الخيانة والكذب.(س).
The impossible in the right of the messengers, peace be upon them. Impossible in their right, peace and blessings be upon them, are the opposites of the obligatory attributes, which are as follows: - Lying: the reality of lying is non-correspondence of the report to what is in actual fact, whether it matches belief or not. - Treachery: by doing something from which they are forbidden by a prohibition of unlawfulness, like adultery and drinking wine, or by a prohibition of dislike, like reciting the Quran in bowing and prostration, for example. As for the occurrence of disliked actions from them, peace be upon them, at some times for legislation, it is permissible. Rather, the disliked action that is impossible for them is that which does not occur with the intention of legislation, for it does not occur from them. So trustworthiness is obligatory for them and treachery is impossible for them. Thus they are infallible from minor and major sins before prophethood and after it. So no forbidden or disliked act occurs from them, neither intentionally nor forgetfully, from the time of their creation until their transition to the abode of honor. Note: It is reported in the hadith: 'Every character trait is imprinted upon the believer except treachery and lying.' (1) The meaning of disliked here includes what is contrary to what is more appropriate. ... (2) And know that there is no difference between minor and major sins; neither minor nor major occurs from them, even forgetfully, before the mission and after it. It cannot be said that what is forgetful or before the mission is not a sin, for we say: it is the form of a sin. And whatever reports give the impression of that occurring from them must be interpreted.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage lists the impossible attributes of prophets: lying and treachery, which are the opposites of truthfulness and trustworthiness. It defines each. It then explains that disliked actions can occur from prophets for the purpose of legislation (to show permissibility), but not as actual undesirable acts. The passage asserts absolute infallibility: prophets are protected from all sins, minor and major, before and after prophethood, intentionally and unintentionally. It cites a hadith to emphasize that treachery and lying are not imprinted on believers, so certainly not on prophets. The commentary also clarifies that any act that appears sinful must be interpreted away.

Correction: The passage defines lying by factual mismatch, not intention.

According to the passage, what is the reality of lying?
A) Saying something false intentionally
B) Non-correspondence of report to reality

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Now think about the 'small' betrayals you tolerate: a broken promise, a hidden fault, a secret compromise. If you are a follower of the prophets, what does your tolerance of these betrayals say about your connection to them? What is one betrayal you will repent of and repair before this week ends?
?

Name one such habit. How does the example of the prophets' intentionality challenge you to either stop it or transform it into something purposeful?

Prophetic Infallibility: Protection from All Sins
Sanusi affirms absolute prophetic infallibility and clarifies the nature of their actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of prophetic infallibility: prophets are protected from all sins, minor and major, before and after prophethood, and that any apparent sinful act must be interpreted.

Core Idea
Prophets are infallible from all sins at all times; no sin occurs from them even forgetfully.

Having established the impossible attributes, Sanusi now declares the consequence: prophets are infallible. This passage affirms that they are protected from minor and major sins before and after prophethood, and that even forgetfulness does not lead to sin. It also cites a hadith and addresses potential objections, emphasizing that any report suggesting otherwise must be reinterpreted.

Guided Path
1
Read the infallibility statement
Read the section that declares prophets are infallible from minor and major sins before and after prophethood, intentionally and forgetfully.
2
Examine the hadith
Note the hadith that every character trait is imprinted on the believer except treachery and lying, reinforcing prophetic purity.
The hadith uses 'believer' but applies strongly to prophets.
3
Understand the scope of acts
The passage explains that prophets' actions are only obligatory or recommended, not permissible in the usual sense.
Even permissible acts are done with intention of worship.
4
Address the objection
The passage answers the objection that forgetfulness or pre-prophethood acts are not sins by stating that they are the form of sin and must be interpreted away.

The Impossible Attributes of Messengers
Lists and explains the attributes impossible for messengers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four attributes that are impossible for messengers and why their impossibility is essential for the credibility of prophethood.

Core Idea
Messengers are divinely protected from all sins and deficiencies, ensuring their perfect trustworthiness.

This lesson examines the attributes that cannot possibly be associated with Allah's messengers. These are the opposites of the obligatory attributes they must possess. Understanding these impossibilities helps us appreciate the divine protection granted to prophets and the reliability of their message.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the four impossible attributes. Notice the author's method of definition and classification.
The passage is structured as a list with clear definitions.
2
Understand each attribute
Work through each of the four attributes: lying, treachery, concealment, stupidity. For each, note the definition and why it is impossible. Pay attention to the nuances, such as the exception for disliked acts done for legislation.
The definition of lying is particularly precise: it does not require intent or belief.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why these impossibilities are necessary for the messengers to fulfill their role. How does this protect the integrity of revelation?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المستحيل في حق الرسل عليهم السلام يستحيل في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام أضداد الصفات الواجبة وهي كما يلي: - الكذب وحقيقة الكذب عدم مطابقة الخبر لما في نفس الأمر سواء وافق الاعتقاد أم لا. - الخيانة: بفعل شيء مما نهوا عنه نهي تحريم كالزنا وشرب الخمر، أو كراهة كقراءة القرآن في الركوع والسجود مثلاً. وأما وقوع المكروه منهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام في بعض الأوقات للتشريع فجائز، وإنما المكروه المستحيل عليهم هو الذي لم يقع بقصد التشريع فإنه لا يقع منهم. فالأمانة واجبة لهم والخيانة مستحيلة عليهم، فهم معصومون من الصغائر والكبائر قبل النبوة وبعدها فلا يقع منهم محرّم ولا مكروه لا عمداً ولا سهواً من حين فطرتهم إلى حين انتقالهم إلى دار الكرامة. - كتمان شيء مما أمروا بتبليغه للخلق المبعوثين إليهم، فهذا مستحيل في حقهم ولا يقع منهم عمداً ولا سهواً. - البلاهة والغباء مستحيلان عليهم صلوات الله تعالى عليهم أجمعين.
The impossible in the right of the messengers, peace be upon them, is impossible in their right, peace and blessings be upon them, the opposites of the obligatory attributes, and they are as follows: - Lying, and the reality of lying is the lack of correspondence of the news with what is in the actual situation, whether it agrees with belief or not. - Treachery: by doing something that they were forbidden from, a prohibition of unlawfulness like adultery and drinking wine, or dislike like reading the Quran in bowing and prostration, for example. As for the occurrence of disliked actions from them, peace and blessings be upon them, at some times for legislation, it is permissible. Indeed, the disliked action that is impossible for them is that which did not occur with the intention of legislation, for it does not occur from them. So trustworthiness is obligatory for them and treachery is impossible for them, for they are infallible from minor and major sins before prophethood and after it, so no forbidden or disliked action occurs from them, neither intentionally nor forgetfully, from the time of their innate nature until their transfer to the abode of honor. - Concealment of something that they were commanded to convey to the creation to whom they were sent, so this is impossible in their right and does not occur from them intentionally or forgetfully. - Stupidity and dullness are impossible for them, may the blessings of Allah the Most High be upon them all.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains four attributes that are impossible (mustaḥīl) for messengers. It begins by stating that these are the opposites of the obligatory attributes. The first is lying (al-kidhb), defined as news not matching reality regardless of belief. The second is treachery (al-khiyānah), which includes both forbidden and disliked acts, though disliked acts done for legislation are permissible. The passage emphasizes that messengers are infallible (maʿṣūmūn) from all sins from birth to death. The third is concealment (kitmān) of the message they were commanded to convey, which is impossible intentionally or forgetfully. The fourth is stupidity and dullness (al-balāhah wa al-ghabāʾ), which are also impossible.

Key Terms
المستحيل
الكذب
الخيانة
العصمة
البلاهة
الغباء
الكتمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think messengers never commit any disliked actions under any circumstances.
Correction: Disliked actions done for legislation are permissible; only those not intended for legislation are impossible.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of lying (al-kidhb) according to the passage?
A) Speaking falsehood intentionally
B) Lack of correspondence between news and reality, whether belief matches or not
C) Acting contrary to divine command
D) Concealing the truth

Key Takeaway
Messengers are divinely protected from lying, treachery, concealment of the message, and stupidity, ensuring their perfect trustworthiness as conveyors of divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage teaches that prophets are never stupid or dull. When you find yourself thinking a prophetic teaching is impractical or outdated, are you doubting their intelligence? How will you train yourself to trust their wisdom over your own reasoning?

The Permissible Human Attributes of Messengers
Enumeration of permissible and impermissible human attributes for messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which human attributes are permissible for messengers and why certain severe defects are excluded.

Core Idea
Messengers can experience minor human frailties, but not repulsive defects.

This lesson explores the concept of what is permissible (jā'iz) for messengers. According to Sunni theology, messengers are human but protected from attributes that would diminish their dignity. The author first defines the category of permissible as temporal accidents, then distinguishes between acceptable human traits and those incompatible with prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Understand the key distinction
Notice how the passage begins by defining permissible attributes as 'accidents' (aʿrāḍ) — created, temporal attributes — in contrast to the eternal attributes that belong only to Allah.
This distinction guards against confusing Creator with creation.
2
Identify permissible and impermissible conditions
Read the list of conditions. Separate those that are permissible (e.g., minor illness, sleep) from those that are not (e.g., leprosy, blindness). Ask yourself why each falls into its category.
The key criterion is whether the condition leads to deficiency or revulsion.
3
Reflect on the theological wisdom
Consider why forgetfulness in prayer is allowed while chronic disease is not. This shows that messengers remain exemplary despite minor human lapses.
Forgetfulness does not detract from their rank; severe illness would.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجائز في حق الرسل عليهم السلام يجوز عقلاً وشرعاً عليهم الصلاة والسلام ما هو من الأعراض أي الصفات الحادثة المتجددة، بعكس الصفات القديمة التي هي صفات الله فلا يصح أن يتصف بها غيره لأن الحادث لا يتصف بصفات القديم. وتجوز على الرسل الصفات البشرية التي لا تؤدي إلى نقص ودناءة في مراتبهم العلية عند الله، كالمرض الخفيف كالحمى والصداع وغير ذلك وأما الأمراض المزمنة كالعقاد والجذام والبرص الذي تعافه الأنفس والجنون قليله وكثيره والعمى والعور وداء الفرج كالجب والاعتراض والخصاء والعُنَّة فلا يجوز في حقهم. ومثل المرض الخفيف أيضا يجوز كالنوم وكذلك الجرح والقتل وإذاية الخلق لهم بالقول والفعل والموتُ والنكاح والطلاق والبيع والشراء والجوع والعطش والسهو في الصلاة فإن هذا كله جائز.
The permissible in the right of the messengers, peace be upon them. Permissible, rationally and legally, for them, prayers and peace be upon them, is that which is from the accidents (al-aʿrāḍ), i.e., the created, renewing attributes, contrary to the eternal attributes which are the attributes of Allah, so it is not correct that other than Him be described with them because the created cannot be described with the attributes of the Eternal. And permissible for the messengers are the human attributes that do not lead to deficiency and lowliness in their lofty ranks with Allah, like minor illness such as fever, headache, and other than that. As for chronic diseases like leprosy (al-juẓām), vitiligo (al-baraṣ) which souls abhor, and insanity in its little and much, blindness, one-eyedness, and genital disease like castration, sterility, and impotence (al-ʿunnah), these are not permissible in their right. And like minor illness, also permissible is sleep, as well as wounding, killing, harming of creation towards them by speech and action, death, marriage, divorce, buying and selling, hunger, thirst, and forgetfulness in prayer, for all of this is permissible.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage explains what is permissible (jāʾiz) for messengers. It begins by stating that permissible things are accidents (aʿrāḍ) — created, temporal attributes — as opposed to eternal attributes that belong only to Allah. Then it specifies that human attributes that do not cause deficiency or lowliness are permissible, such as minor illnesses (fever, headache). However, chronic or repulsive diseases are not permissible. The passage lists several impermissible conditions: leprosy, vitiligo, insanity, blindness, one-eyedness, genital defects, etc. Then it lists permissible things: sleep, wounding, being killed, harm from others, death, marriage, divorce, trade, hunger, thirst, and forgetfulness in prayer. The key is that these do not detract from their high status.

الأعراض
الصفات الحادثة
الصفات القديمة
المزمنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think messengers cannot have any human weaknesses or imperfections.
Correction: The passage clarifies that minor ailments and forgetfulness are permissible; only severe, repulsive defects are excluded.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT permissible for messengers according to the passage?
A) Minor illness like headache
B) Forgetfulness in prayer
C) Chronic disease like leprosy
D) Sleep

Key Takeaway
Messengers are human but protected from attributes that would cause revulsion or severe deficiency; minor human experiences are permissible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If messengers experienced minor illnesses and forgetfulness, does that challenge your assumption that spiritual rank eliminates all human trials? When you face a small setback, do you see it as a chance to be elevated like them, or as a sign of failure?
?
The passage says messengers cannot have repulsive defects. How does that affect the way you speak about the Prophet (peace be upon him) or other messengers? Are there any jokes or casual remarks you've made that contradict their dignity?
?
Forgetfulness in prayer was permissible for them. When you make a mistake in your worship, do you despair or remember that even the best of creation had such moments? Will you commit to forgiving yourself and continuing with humility?

Obligations of Prophets and Messengers
Sanusi clarifies obligations of prophets versus messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all obligations of messengers apply to prophets except the command to convey, and that prophets must announce their prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophets share all messenger obligations except tablīgh, but must announce themselves.

Sanusi first addresses a common question: Are prophets who are not messengers bound by the same duties? He clarifies that they are, except for the specific command to deliver revelation. However, they still have a duty to make their prophethood known to receive proper respect. This distinction is important for understanding the hierarchy of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on obligations
Read the first part of the Arabic passage (up to the footnote marker) and its translation. Notice the universal statement that all messenger obligations apply to prophets.
The exception is tablīgh (conveying) since prophets not sent as messengers are not commanded to convey.
2
Identify the exception and additional duty
Find the exception: tablīgh is not obligatory for non-messenger prophets. Then note the additional duty: a prophet must inform people he is a prophet so they respect him.
This respect is a practical necessity, not a theological requirement.
3
Reflect on the distinction
Ask yourself why Sanusi makes this clarification. It prevents confusion about the roles of prophets vs. messengers and emphasizes the honor due to all prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل ما وجب للرسل واجب للأنبياء الذين لم يرسلوا للتبليغ للخلق فإنهم لم يؤمروا به، لكن يجب على النبي أن يخبر الناس أنه نبي ليحترمه الناس. (۱) السهو في التبليغ مستحيل، وأما في غيره فجائز فقد سها عليه الصلاة والسلام في الصلاة لكن باشتغال قلبه العظيم الله وإلى هذا المعنى أشار بعضهم. يا سائلي عن رسول الله كيف سها قد غاب عن كل شيء سره فسها
And everything that is obligatory for the messengers is obligatory for the prophets who were not sent to convey to the creation, for they were not commanded with it. But it is obligatory for the prophet to inform the people that he is a prophet so that people respect him. (1) Forgetfulness in conveying is impossible, but in other than that it is permissible, for he, peace and blessings be upon him, forgot in prayer, but due to the preoccupation of his great heart with Allah. And to this meaning some have alluded: 'O you who ask about the Messenger of Allah, how did he forget? His secret was absent from everything, so he forgot.'
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage draws a distinction between prophets and messengers. It states that all obligations of messengers are also obligations for prophets (anbiyāʾ) who were not sent as messengers, except the command to convey (tablīgh). However, a prophet must still announce his prophethood so people respect him. Then it addresses forgetfulness (sahw): forgetfulness in conveying the message is impossible (mustaḥīl), but in other matters, such as prayer, it is permissible. The Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) forgot in prayer, but this was due to his heart being absorbed in Allah. A poetic verse is cited to illustrate that his forgetfulness was from being so focused on Allah that he was absent from other matters.

Forgetfulness of the Prophet in Prayer
Sanusi discusses the permissibility of forgetfulness for prophets in non-conveying matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that forgetfulness in conveying the message is impossible for prophets, but forgetfulness in other acts like prayer is permissible due to absorption in Allah.

Core Idea
Prophetic forgetfulness is impossible in revelation, but possible in prayer due to spiritual absorption.

Sanusi now addresses a delicate topic: the Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer. He first makes a clear distinction: forgetfulness in conveying the message (tablīgh) is impossible because that would compromise revelation. However, in other matters, such as prayer, it is permissible. He then explains that the Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer was not from carelessness but from his heart being completely absorbed in the greatness of Allah. A poetic verse is cited to illustrate this state.

Guided Path
1

The verse is a poetic explanation of the Prophet's state.
2
Identify the two categories
The passage distinguishes between forgetfulness in tablīgh (impossible) and in other matters (permissible). The example given is forgetfulness in prayer.
3
Understand the reason for forgetfulness in prayer
The Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer is attributed to his heart being preoccupied with Allah. The verse illustrates that his 'secret' (deep spiritual focus) was so absorbed that he forgot worldly matters.
This shows the forgetfulness was not a deficiency but a sign of profound devotion.

The Impossible for Prophets
Enumeration of impossibilities for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific attributes and actions that are impossible for prophets, including concealment of revelation and certain physical and mental defects.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from concealing revelation and from repulsive defects.

This lesson explores the category of impossible attributes for prophets. The author begins with the most fundamental: concealment of any part of the divine message. He then quotes al-Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ to include leprosy, madness, and stupidity, clarifying a common misconception about Prophet Ayyūb.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author states the rule for concealment and then adds a note quoting al-Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ.
The passage is concise but contains a clear list.
2
Identify the list of impossibilities
From the passage, extract all the items that are said to be impossible for prophets. There are at least five.
Remember the clarification about Prophet Ayyūb.
3
Understand the scope of concealment
The first impossibility is concealment of the message—this covers both intentional and forgetful omission. Reflect on why this is fundamental for prophethood.
4
Note the clarification about Prophet Ayyūb
The passage explicitly states that what happened to Prophet Ayyūb was not leprosy. This corrects a common misunderstanding.
Al-Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ is the source of this clarification.
5
Reflect on why these are impossible

كتمان شيء مما أمروا بتبليغه للخلق المبعوثين إليهم، فهذا مستحيل في حقهم ولا يقع منهم عمداً ولا سهوا. ملاحظة : قال القاضي عياض في الشفاء : وكذا يستحيل عليهم الجنون والجذام والبرص، وما كان لسيدنا أيوب ليس بجذام. البلاهة والغباء مستحيلان عليهم صلوات الله تعالى عليهم أجمعين.

Commentary
This passage defines what is impossible (mustaḥīl) for prophets. Finally, it states that stupidity and dullness are impossible for all prophets.

Permissible Human Attributes for Prophets
Sanusi enumerates permissible and impermissible human attributes for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which human attributes and actions are permissible for prophets and why, and the distinction between mild and chronic/repulsive conditions.

Core Idea
Prophets are human but free from defects that degrade their rank.

The author explains that prophets can experience human attributes that do not lower their status, such as mild illness and normal human acts, but not severe or repulsive diseases. This passage clarifies the boundaries of prophetic humanity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall content.
Notice the detailed list of permissible and impermissible items.
2
Identify the two categories of attributes
The passage distinguishes between accidents (created, renewing attributes) and eternal attributes (only for Allah). Permissible for prophets are accidents that do not cause deficiency.
This is a key theological principle.
3
List permissible and impermissible attributes
Find examples of mild illnesses, actions, and chronic diseases. Categorise them as permissible or impermissible based on the text.
Chronic includes leprosy, madness, blindness, etc.
4
Understand forgetfulness
The passage specifies that forgetfulness in conveying the message is impossible, but in other matters (like prayer) it is permissible. The Prophet's forgetfulness was due to his absorption in Allah.
This shows prophetic infallibility in transmission.
5
Reflect on the wisdom
Consider why these distinctions exist: prophets must be relatable yet revered. Chronic diseases would repulse people and hinder their mission.
This connects to the purpose of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجائز في حق الرسل عليهم السلام يجوز عقلاً وشرعاً عليهم الصلاة والسلام ما هو من الأعراض أي الصفات الحادثة المتجددة، بعكس الصفات القديمة التي هي صفات الله فلا يصح أن يتصف بها غيره لأن الحادث لا يتصف بصفات القديم. وتجوز على الرسل الصفات البشرية التي لا تؤدي إلى نقص ودناءة في مراتبهم العلية عند الله ، كالمرض الخفيف كالحمى والصداع وغير ذلك وأما الأمراض المزمنة كالعقاد والجذام والبرص الذي تعافه الأنفس والجنون قليله وكثيره والعمى والعور وداء الفرج كالجب والاعتراض والخصاء والعُنَّة فلا يجوز في حقهم. ومثل المرض الخفيف أيضا يجوز كالنوم وكذلك الجرح والقتل وإذاية الخلق لهم بالقول والفعل والموتُ والنكاح والطلاق والبيع والشراء والجوع والعطش والسهو في الصلاة فإن هذا كله جائز. وكل ما وجب للرسل واجب للأنبياء الذين لم يرسلوا للتبليغ للخلق فإنهم لم يؤمروا به ، لكن يجب على النبي أن يخبر الناس أنه نبي ليحترمه الناس. (١) السهو في التبليغ مستحيل ، وأما في غيره فجائز فقد سها عليه الصلاة والسلام في الصلاة لكن باشتغال قلبه العظيم الله وإلى هذا المعنى أشار بعضهم . يا سائلي عن رسول الله كيف سها قد غاب عن كل شيء سره فسها والسهو من كل قلب غافل لاهي عما سوى الله العظيم الله
What is permissible (jāʾiz) concerning the messengers, peace be upon them: It is rationally and legally permissible for them, blessings and peace be upon them, that which is of the accidents (aʿrāḍ), i.e., the created, renewing attributes, as opposed to the eternal attributes which are the attributes of Allāh—so it is not correct that anyone other than Him should be described with them, because the created being (al-ḥādith) is not described with the attributes of the Eternal (al-qadīm). And permissible for the messengers are human attributes that do not lead to deficiency and lowliness in their lofty ranks with Allāh, such as mild illness like fever and headache and so forth. As for chronic diseases such as 'al-ʿiqād', leprosy, vitiligo which souls detest, madness both slight and severe, blindness, one-eyedness, genital disease like impotence (al-jabb), al-iʿtirāḍ, castration, and al-ʿunna—these are not permissible concerning them. And likewise, mild illness is permissible, such as sleep, as well as wounding, being killed, harm from people to them by speech and action, death, marriage, divorce, selling, buying, hunger, thirst, and forgetfulness (sahw) in prayer—all of this is permissible. And everything that is obligatory for messengers is obligatory for prophets who were not sent for conveying to creation—for they were not commanded with it—but it is necessary for a prophet to inform people that he is a prophet so that people may respect him. (1) Forgetfulness in conveying the message is impossible, but in other matters it is permissible. Indeed, he, peace and blessings be upon him, forgot in prayer, but due to his great heart being occupied with Allāh. And to this meaning some have alluded: 'O you who ask me about the Messenger of Allāh, how could he forget? He was absent from everything except his secret, so he forgot. And forgetfulness comes only from a heart that is heedless and unmindful of everything besides Allāh, the Mighty.'
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage details what is permissible (jāʾiz) for messengers from human attributes. It divides attributes into two categories: accidents (aʿrāḍ)—which are created and renewing—and eternal attributes which belong solely to Allāh. Permissible human traits are those that do not cause deficiency in the prophet's rank, such as mild illness (fever, headache) and sleep. Chronic or repulsive diseases are not permissible. Specific examples are given: leprosy, vitiligo, madness, blindness, etc. Permissible actions include being wounded, killed, harmed by others, death, marriage, divorce, trade, hunger, thirst, and forgetfulness in prayer. Then the author explains that what is obligatory for messengers is also obligatory for prophets who were not sent with a mission, but they must still announce their prophethood. A footnote clarifies that forgetfulness in conveying the message is impossible, but forgetfulness in other matters is permissible; the Prophet's forgetfulness in prayer was due to his heart being absorbed in contemplation of Allāh, not from heedlessness.

أعراض
صفات حادثة
الأمراض المزمنة
السهو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all human ailments are permissible for prophets.
Correction: Chronic/repulsive diseases like leprosy, madness, and blindness are not permissible because they cause deficiency and repulsion.

Key Takeaway

Christian and Jewish extremes regarding prophets
The author contrasts Christian excess and Jewish deficiency in their views of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Christians went to excess in deifying Jesus and how the Jews fell short in respecting prophets, according to the author's critique.

Core Idea
The golden mean in prophetic veneration avoids Christian excess and Jewish deficiency.

The author points out two opposite errors: Christians raised Jesus to divinity, while Jews described prophets with unbecoming qualities. These extremes highlight the balanced Islamic view of prophets as honored servants of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the two notes carefully
Read the Arabic passage for both notes together. Notice the parallel structure: first the Christian error, then the Jewish error.
2
Identify the Christian claim
What exactly did the Christians claim about Jesus? They said he is the attribute of eternal knowledge subsisting in his body, making him a god.
This is a rational impossibility according to Islamic theology.
3
Identify the Jewish error
What did the Jews do? They described prophets in ways that are unbecoming of them, falling short of proper respect.
The contrast shows the importance of the middle path.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Think about why the author presents these two errors together. How does this protect the correct belief about prophets?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملاحظة : النصارى وصفوا النبي عيسى عليه السلام بصفات الله فزعموا أنه صفة العلم القديمة قائمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام وجعلوه لذلك إلها على خبط لهم عظيم لا يفوه به عاقل. ملاحظة : اليهود وصفوا الأنبياء بالأمور التي لا تليق بهم، فالنصارى أفرطوا فرفعوا عيسى فوق حقه إلى قولهم إنه ابن الله واليهود فرطوا. ملاحظة : ما ذكر عن النبي شعيب أنه كان ضريرا لم يثبت كما ذكره المحققون وأما يعقوب عليه السلام فحصلت له غشاوة ولم تمنعه النظر ثم زالت عنه ، وأما بلاء أيوب فلم تعفه النفس ولم يستقر به بل صار بدنه بعد الشفاء أجمل منه قبل.
Note: The Christians described the Prophet Jesus, peace be upon him, with the attributes of Allāh, claiming that he is the attribute of eternal knowledge subsisting in the body of Jesus, and thereby made him a god—a great confusion that no sane person would utter. Note: The Jews described the prophets with matters unbecoming of them. Thus the Christians went to excess, raising Jesus beyond his right to the extent of saying he is the son of God, and the Jews fell short. Note: What has been mentioned about the Prophet Shuʿayb being blind has not been confirmed, as the investigators have stated. As for Yaʿqūb, peace be upon him, a veil came over him but it did not prevent his sight, then it lifted. As for the trial of Ayyūb, it did not make the soul loathe him nor did it persist; rather, his body after recovery became more beautiful than before.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage highlights three corrections regarding prophets. First, Christians wrongly attribute divine attributes to Jesus, considering him as the eternal attribute of knowledge incarnate and thus a god—an irrational confusion. Second, Jews describe prophets with unbecoming qualities, while Christians go to excess by calling Jesus son of God. The contrast shows the golden mean in prophetic veneration. Third, three historical claims are corrected: Shuʿayb was not blind; Yaʿqūb had a temporary veil that did not prevent sight; and Ayyūb's affliction was not repulsive and he became even more beautiful after recovery.

The author corrects three false historical claims about prophets Shu'ayb, Ya'qub, and Ayyub.

False historical claims about prophets are corrected with evidence from investigators.

The author addresses three specific false beliefs about prophets: that Shu'ayb was blind, that Ya'qub lost his sight completely, and that Ayyub's body became repulsive. He clarifies each based on scholarly investigation.

The Sleep of Prophets: Eyes Sleep, Hearts Awake
The author compiles multiple hadith proving that prophets' eyes sleep while their hearts remain awake.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets experience physical sleep while their hearts remain fully conscious, as proven by authentic hadith.

Core Idea
Prophets' eyes sleep, but their hearts never do.

In this lesson, we explore a unique characteristic of prophets: their physical eyes rest in sleep, but their hearts remain awake and aware. This is established through multiple authentic hadith narrated from the Prophet ﷺ and his companions. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full translation. Notice the multiple narrations gathered.
The passage begins with a note from the author about the authenticity.
2
Identify the core claim
The central claim is that prophets' eyes sleep but their hearts do not. This is stated explicitly in several hadith.
The claim is repeated by different narrators.
3
Trace the hadith chains
Notice the variety of narrators: Aisha, Anas ibn Malik, Ibn Abbas, and others. This shows the claim is well-attested.
Each hadith chain reinforces the same point.
4
Reflect on the significance
Why does this matter? It shows prophets are fully human physically but their hearts are always connected to Allah, even in sleep.
This distinguishes them from ordinary humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملاحظة : الأنبياء تنام أعينهم ولا تنام قلوبهم ) إما غالباً أو دائماً وهذا صححه الإمام النووي. رواه البخاري في صحيحه عن أبي سلمة بن عبد الرحمن أنه سأل عائشة ـ رضي الله تعالى عنها - كيف كانت صلاة رسول الله له الله في رمضان قالت ما كان يزيد في رمضان ولا غيره على إحدى عشرة ركعة يصلي أربع ركعات فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلي أربعاً فلا تسأل عن حسنهن وطولهن ثم يصلي ثلاثاً فقلت: يا رسول الله تنام قبل أن توتر قال تنام عيني ولا ينام قلبي. ورواه البخاري أيضاً عن شريك بن عبد الله بن أبي نمر : ' سمعت أنس بن مالك يحدثنا عن ليلة أسري بالنبي الاول من مسجد الكعبة جاء ثلاثة نفر قبل أن يوحى إليه وهو نائم في مسجد الحرام ، فقال أولهم أيهم هو فقال أوسطهم هو خيرهم ، وقال آخرهم خذوا خيرهم فكانت تلك ، فلم يرهم حتى جاؤوا ليلة أخرى فيما يرى قلبه والنبي نائمة عيناه ولا ينام قلبه وكذلك الأنبياء تنام أعينهم ولا تنام قلوبهم فتولاه جبريل ثم عرج به إلى السماء'. وروى النسائي في سننه الكبرى عن سعيد بن جبير عن ابن عباس قال أقبلت يهود إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالوا يا أبا القاسم نسألك عن أشياء فإن أجبتنا فيها اتبعناك وصدقناك وآمنا بك قال فأخذ عليهم ما أخذ إسرائيل على بنيه إذ قالوا الله على ما نقول وكيل قال أخبرنا عن علامة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال تنام عيناه ولا ينام قلبه ... إلخ. ورواه عنه أيضا الطبراني في المعجم الكبير. وروى البيهقي في سننه الكبرى عن عائشة في حديث ذكره في صلاة الليل قالت : فقلت يا رسول الله تنام قبل أن توتر فقال : يا عائشة إن عيني تنامان ولا ينام قلبي قال : رواه البخاري في الصحيح عن القعنبي ورواه مسلم عن يحيى بن يحيى عن مالك وروينا عن جابر بن عبد الله وأبي هريرة وأنس بن مالك عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ما دل على أنه كان تنام عيناه ولا ينام قلبه قال أنس بن مالك وكذلك الأنبياء صلوات الله عليهم تنام أعينهم ولا تنام قلوبهم. وروى الحاكم في مستدركه عن أنس - رضي الله تعالى عنه - قال : ' كان النبي تنام عيناه ولا ينام قلبه' هذا حديث صحيح على شرط مسلم ولم يخرجاه.
Note: The prophets sleep in their eyes but their hearts do not sleep—either usually or always, and this was authenticated by Imām al-Nawawī. Al-Bukhārī narrated in his Ṣaḥīḥ from Abū Salama ibn ʿAbd al-Raḥmān that he asked ʿĀʾisha—may Allāh be pleased with her—how the prayer of the Messenger of Allāh (ﷺ) was in Ramaḍān. She said: He did not increase in Ramaḍān or otherwise beyond eleven rakʿahs. He would pray four—do not ask about their beauty and length—then pray four—do not ask about their beauty and length—then pray three. I said: O Messenger of Allāh, do you sleep before praying witr? He said: My eye sleeps but my heart does not sleep. And al-Bukhārī also narrated from Sharīk ibn ʿAbd Allāh ibn Abī Namir: 'I heard Anas ibn Mālik narrating to us about the night when the Prophet (ﷺ) was taken on the Night Journey from the Mosque of the Kaʿbah: Three figures came before he received revelation while he was asleep in the Sacred Mosque. The first said: Which of them is he? The middle one said: He is the best of them. The last said: Take the best of them. That was that. He did not see them until they came another night, according to what his heart saw—the Prophet's eyes were asleep but his heart was not asleep. And likewise, the prophets' eyes sleep but their hearts do not sleep. Then Jibrīl took charge of him and ascended with him to heaven.' And al-Nasāʾī narrated in his Sunan al-Kubrā from Saʿīd ibn Jubayr from Ibn ʿAbbās: 'Jews came to the Prophet (ﷺ) and said: O Abū al-Qāsim, we ask you about things. If you answer us, we will follow you, believe you, and have faith in you. He said: He took from them what Israel took from his sons when they said: Allāh is a witness to what we say. He said: Inform us about the sign of the Prophet (ﷺ). He said: His eyes sleep but his heart does not sleep... etc.' And al-Ṭabarānī also narrated it from him in al-Muʿjam al-Kabīr. And al-Bayhaqī narrated in his Sunan al-Kubrā from ʿĀʾisha in a ḥadīth he mentioned about night prayer: She said: I said: O Messenger of Allāh, do you sleep before praying witr? He said: O ʿĀʾisha, my eyes sleep but my heart does not sleep. He said: Al-Bukhārī narrated it in al-Ṣaḥīḥ from al-Qaʿnabī, and Muslim narrated it from Yaḥyā ibn Yaḥyā from Mālik. And we narrated from Jābir ibn ʿAbd Allāh, Abū Hurayra, and Anas ibn Mālik from the Prophet (ﷺ) that which indicates that his eyes slept but his heart did not sleep. Anas ibn Mālik said: Likewise the prophets, blessings of Allāh be upon them, their eyes sleep but their hearts do not sleep. And al-Ḥākim narrated in al-Mustadrak from Anas—may Allāh be pleased with him—that he said: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) slept in his eyes but his heart did not sleep.' This ḥadīth is ṣaḥīḥ according to the condition of Muslim, but they did not record it.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage provides the hadith evidence that prophets' eyes sleep but their hearts do not. It begins with a note that this is either usually or always the case, authenticated by al-Nawawī. Then multiple narrations are cited: from ʿĀʾisha (about sleep before witr), from Anas (about the Night Journey), from Ibn ʿAbbās (Jews asking about the sign of the Prophet), and from various other chains. All confirm that the Prophet's physical eyes sleep but his heart remains awake, and this is a characteristic of all prophets. The passage thus establishes a unique state for prophets that combines human physical rest with constant spiritual awareness.

?

?

?
The Jews asked for a sign of a true prophet, and the answer was a heart that never sleeps. Does your own heart bear that sign? If not, what will you change tonight to make your heart more alive to Allah than your body is to the world?

Prophethood

Textual Proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma
Sanusi presents three textual proofs for the truthfulness of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the truthfulness of prophets is established through three textual sources: the Quran, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the Muslim community.

Core Idea
The truthfulness of prophets is proven by revelation and unanimous agreement.

In this passage, Sanusi presents the scriptural and communal evidences for the truthfulness of messengers. The Quran directly attests to the Prophet's truthfulness, the Sunnah records his own affirmation, and the consensus of scholars confirms this belief. Let us examine each proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the three distinct sources: the Quran, the Sunnah, and Ijma (consensus).
The passage begins with a topic statement, then enumerates each source with evidence.
2
Study the Quranic verses
Three verses are cited. Read each one and understand how it indicates the Prophet's truthfulness. The first verse shows his speech is revelation, the second implies there are truthful people, and the third directly states truthfulness.
The verses are from Surat al-Najm and Surat al-Ahzab.
3
Understand the Sunnah and Ijma proofs
The hadith quotes the Prophet denying negative traits, implying his truthfulness. The consensus states that all Muslims agree on the obligation of prophets' truthfulness. Reflect on why consensus is a binding proof.
Consensus (Ijma) is a primary source of Islamic law and theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على إثبات الصدق للرسل من جهة النقل الكتاب والسنة والإجماع أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى في حق نبينا قال تعالى: (وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْى يُوحَى) [النجم: 3-4]، وقوله تعالى: (لِيَسْتَلَ الصَّدِقِينَ عَن صِدْقِهِمْ) [الأحزاب: 8]، وقوله تعالى: (وَصَدَقَ اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ) [الأحزاب: 22]. والسنة قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم "لا تجدوني بخيلاً ولا كذوباً ولا جباناً". وأما الإجماع فقد أجمع المسلمون على وجوب صدق الرسل والأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام.
And the textual proof for establishing truthfulness for the messengers is the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. As for the Book, His statement, exalted is He, regarding our Prophet, He said: 'Nor does he speak from [his own] inclination. It is not but a revelation revealed.' [al-Najm 53:3-4], and His statement: 'That Allah may question the truthful about their truthfulness' [al-Ahzab 33:8], and His statement: 'And Allah and His Messenger are truthful' [al-Ahzab 33:22]. And as for the Sunnah, his statement, peace and blessings be upon him: 'You will not find me miserly, nor a liar, nor cowardly.' And as for consensus, the Muslims have agreed upon the necessity of the truthfulness of the messengers and prophets, peace and blessings be upon them.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents the textual proofs for the truthfulness of the messengers. It is a classification of evidence from three sources: the Quran, the Sunnah, and Ijma (consensus). For the Quran, three verses are cited: First, 'Nor does he speak from desire; it is only a revelation revealed' (al-Najm 53:3-4), indicating that the Prophet's speech is not his own but from Allah, so it is truthful. Second, 'That Allah may question the truthful about their truthfulness' (al-Ahzab 33:8), implying that there are truthful individuals. Third, 'And Allah and His Messenger are truthful' (al-Ahzab 33:22), directly stating truthfulness. For the Sunnah, a hadith is quoted where the Prophet says, 'You will not find me miserly, nor a liar, nor cowardly,' implying his truthfulness. For Ijma, the passage states that all Muslims agree on the obligation of the truthfulness of the messengers and prophets. This consensus is a binding source in Islamic theology. Thus, the truthfulness of prophets is affirmed by revelation and community agreement.

Key Terms
كتاب
سنة
إجماع
صدق الرسل
وحي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think these proofs are only for Prophet Muhammad.
Correction: The verses and consensus apply to all prophets, as indicated by the general terms 'messengers' and 'prophets' in the Ijma statement.

Checkpoint
Which source is NOT cited as textual proof for the truthfulness of messengers in this passage?

B) The Sunnah
C) Qiyas (analogical reasoning)
D) Ijma (consensus)

Key Takeaway
The truthfulness of messengers is established by Quranic verses, a prophetic hadith, and unanimous consensus of the Muslim community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet declared he is not a liar. When you follow his commands, do you do so with complete trust, or do you hold back because of doubts about their relevance?
?
Consensus of Muslims affirms the truthfulness of all prophets. Does the collective testimony of the Ummah strengthen your own belief, or do you rely solely on your personal reasoning?

Prophethood

Classification of Extraordinary Events
Sanusi defines miracle and classifies other extraordinary events by their relationship to prophethood and sanctity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spectrum of extraordinary events in Islamic theology — from miracles to deceptive trials — and how they relate to prophethood, sainthood, and divine agency.

Core Idea
Extraordinary events are divine signs that vary based on who performs them and why.

Sanusi presents a precise taxonomy of extraordinary events (khawariq al-‘adah) that is essential for distinguishing authentic prophethood from false claims. This passage defines the miracle (mu‘jizah) as a challenged and unmatched sign, and then systematically classifies other wonders by their relationship to prophethood, holiness, and divine purpose. It also clarifies that sorcery and jugglery, having mundane causes, are not genuine khawariq.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions of mu'jizah and karamah
Notice how both are khawariq but distinguished by their link to prophethood. A miracle accompanies a challenge and a claim of prophethood, while karamah is for saints without such a claim.
2
Explore the remaining five types
Identify irhas, i'anah, istidraj, ihanah, and ibtila'. Note the key contrast: some happen to believers (i'anah), some to disbelievers/sinners (istidraj, ihanah), and ibtila' is a trial from misleaders.
The example of Musaylimah illustrates ihanah.
3
Understand the exclusion of sorcery
Sorcery and sha'wadhah are not khawariq because they have learned causes. The passage reaffirms that all genuine khawariq are directly by Allah's power alone.
4
Reflect on divine agency
The final statement emphasizes that human beings have no causal effect in these events; Allah is the sole agent. This is a key Ash'ari theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملاحظة : حقيقة المعجزة أمر خارق للعادة مقرون بالتحدي مع عدم المعارضة. ملاحظة : الكرامة هي أمر خارق للعادة غير مقرون بدعوى النبوة ولا مقدمة لها. وهي للأولياء، فالمقرون بدعوى النبوة معجزة والمقدمة لها إرهاص فإنه للأنبياء سابق على دعوى النبوة كتظليل الغمام له، وإعانة وهي ما تقع لبعض عوام المؤمنين الذين لم يصلوا لمرتبة الولاية تخليصاً لهم من المحن والمهالك. واستدراج وهو ما يقع لبعض الكفرة والفسقة مطابقة لمرادهم. وإهانة وهي ما تقع للفساق والكفرة أيضاً مخالفة لمرادهم كما وقع المسيلمة الكذاب أنه بزق في بئر ليزداد حلاوة فصار ملحاً أجاجاً. وابتلاء وهو ما يحصل على يد من يريد إضلال الخلق كالدجال مثلا. وأما السحر والشعوذة فليسا من الخوارق لأن لهما أسباباً تتعلم. وهذه الخوارق لا تأثير للعباد فيها وإنما الفاعل هو الله وحده.
Note: The reality of the miracle (mu'jizah) is an extraordinary matter accompanied by a challenge with no opposition. Note: The karamah is an extraordinary matter not accompanied by a claim of prophethood nor a precursor to it. It is for saints (awliya'). So what is accompanied by a claim of prophethood is a miracle; and what is a precursor to it is irhas (preparatory marvel), for it is for prophets before the claim of prophethood, like the cloud shading him. And i'anah (assistance) is what occurs for some common believers who have not reached the rank of sainthood, to deliver them from trials and perils. And istidraj (gradual entrapment) is what occurs for some disbelievers and sinners in accordance with their desire. And ihanah (disgrace) is what occurs for sinners and disbelievers contrary to their desire, as happened to the liar Musaylimah when he spat into a well to increase its sweetness, but it became salty and bitter. And ibtila' (trial) is what occurs at the hands of one who wishes to mislead people, like the Dajjal for example. As for sorcery (sihr) and jugglery (sha'wadhah), they are not among the extraordinary events because they have causes that are learned. And these extraordinary events have no effect from the servants; rather, the agent is Allah alone.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed classification of extraordinary events (khawariq al-'adah). It begins by defining the true miracle (mu'jizah) as an extraordinary occurrence accompanied by a challenge (tahaddi) to produce something similar, with no successful opposition. It is a sign of prophethood. Then it defines karamah (wonder) as an extraordinary event for a saint (wali) that is not linked to a claim of prophethood. The passage then lists and distinguishes other types: irhas (preparatory marvel) happens to prophets before their claim, like the cloud shading the Prophet Muhammad before his prophethood; i'anah (assistance) happens to ordinary believers to save them from harm; istidraj (gradual entrapment) happens to disbelievers and sinners in accordance with their wishes, leading them further into error; ihanah (disgrace) happens to sinners and disbelievers contrary to their wishes, as a humiliation, exemplified by the false prophet Musaylimah's failed miracle; ibtila' (trial) happens at the hands of those who seek to mislead people, like the Dajjal. The passage also clarifies that sorcery and sleight-of-hand are not extraordinary because they are learned skills with natural causes. Finally, it emphasizes that all these events are created by Allah alone; humans have no causal power over them.

Key Terms
معجزة
كرامة
إرهاص
إعانة
استدراج
إهانة
ابتلاء
سحر
شعوذة
خوارق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that karamah is the same as mu'jizah or that sorcery is a supernatural wonder.
Correction: The passage clarifies that karamah is for saints without a claim of prophethood, while mu'jizah is for prophets with a challenge. Sorcery has learned causes and is not truly supernatural.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes a miracle (mu'jizah) from a karamah?
A) A karamah is accompanied by a challenge, a miracle is not.
B) A miracle is accompanied by a claim of prophethood, a karamah is not.
C) A miracle occurs for saints, a karamah for prophets.
D) They are the same thing.

Key Takeaway
Extraordinary events are divine acts that serve as signs of prophethood, sainthood, or divine will, all created by Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When something extraordinary happens in your life, do you immediately attribute it to your own effort or to Allah? How does this lesson's statement that 'the agent is Allah alone' challenge your natural pride? Will you begin consciously saying 'Allah alone did this' even in small successes?
?
Think of a time you received something you strongly desired but later realized it was harmful. Could that have been istidraj? If so, what does that reveal about the state of your heart? Are you willing to ask Allah to save you from being trapped by your own wants?

Evidence for the Truthfulness of Messengers from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma'
Sanusi cites three sources proving the obligation of truthfulness for messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three classical proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma') that establish the obligation of truthfulness for messengers.

Core Idea
Three sources prove messengers are truthful.

In this lesson, we examine the concise yet powerful passage where Sanusi presents the three textual proofs for the truthfulness of messengers. These proofs form the foundation for believing in the reliability of prophetic messages.

3

Definition of Miracles (Mu'jizah)
Sanusi defines the miracle with four conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of a miracle in Islamic theology and its four necessary conditions.

Core Idea
A miracle is a divine proof: extraordinary, challenged, and unmatched.

Sanusi gives a tight definition of the miracle (mu'jizah) as the key proof of prophethood. This passage lays out the four conditions that distinguish a true miracle from other extraordinary events. Understanding these conditions is essential for recognizing the signs of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice how compact the definition is.
2
Identify the four conditions
Break the definition into its components: an event (amr), extraordinary (khariq lil-'adah), paired with a challenge (tahaddi), and no opposition (mu'aradah).
The fourth condition is stated as 'with no opposition' (ma'a 'adam al-mu'aradah).
3
Reflect on the role of challenge and opposition
Ask yourself why a miracle must include a challenge and why the lack of opposition is crucial. These conditions ensure that only a true prophet can perform a miracle.
This connects to the broader topic of prophethood proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملاحظة : حقيقة المعجزة أمر خارق للعادة مقرون بالتحدي مع عدم المعارضة.
Note: The reality of the miracle is an event that breaks the norm, paired with a challenge, and without opposition.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage gives a concise definition of mu'jizah (miracle) as a proof of prophethood. It has four conditions: it is an event (amr) that is extraordinary (khariq lil-‘adah), meaning it violates the normal course of nature; it is accompanied by a challenge (tahaddi) from the prophet claiming prophethood; and there is no opposition (mu‘aradah) from others to produce something similar. A miracle is thus distinguished from other extraordinary events.

Correction: The conditions of challenge and lack of opposition ensure that miracles are exclusive to true prophets, as no impostor can fulfill both.

?
