Types of Extraordinary Events and Their Divine Origin
Sanusi enumerates types of extraordinary events and their divine source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different types of extraordinary events (khawariq al-‘adah) and why only Allah produces them.

Core Idea
All extraordinary events come from Allah alone; they reveal His power through prophets, saints, or as trials.

Sanusi provides a precise classification of events that break natural norms. He distinguishes miracles of prophets, wonders for saints, and deceptive occurrences for disbelievers. This lesson will help you navigate these categories and understand that none of them are caused by created beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the full classification.
Notice the structure: definition of karama, then list of related types, then exclusion of sihr/sha'wadhah, then theological conclusion.
2
Identify and define each type
List each type of khawariq mentioned: karama, mu'jiza, irhas, i'anah, istidraj, ihanah, ibtila'. Note their definitions and examples.
Pay attention to the distinction between mu'jiza and irhas: one accompanies prophecy, the other precedes it.
3
Distinguish khawariq from sihr and sha'wadhah
Sanusi explicitly excludes sihr and sha'wadhah from khawariq because they have learnable causes. Understand why this distinction matters for theology.
This guards against attributing supernatural power to creatures.
4
Reflect on the theological conclusion
The passage ends with the statement that all khawariq have no effect from creatures; Allah alone is the agent. Consider the implications for understanding divine power.
This reinforces tawhid al-af‘al (oneness of divine actions).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed classification of extraordinary events (khawariq al-‘adah). The author first defines karama (saintly miracle) and then distinguishes various types: mu'jizah (prophetic miracle), irhas (preparatory wonder for prophets), i‘anah (divine assistance for ordinary believers), istidraj (gradual deception for disbelievers), ihanah (humiliation for the wicked), and ibtila' (trial, like the Dajjal's magic-like phenomena). He clarifies that sihr and sha'wadhah are not khawariq because they have learnable causes. Crucially, he affirms that all these events are produced solely by Allah, not by any created being. This classification is important for distinguishing authentic miracles from false claims.

Proof of the Obligation of Trustworthiness for Messengers
Sanusi proves messengers' trustworthiness via the command to follow them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that messengers must be trustworthy and how the command to follow them implies their actions cannot be sinful.

Core Idea
A messenger’s sin would become obedience for us—impossible, therefore messengers are sinless.

Sanusi presents a concise rational argument for the necessary trustworthiness of messengers. If a messenger could commit a sin, that sin would become an act of worship for us because we are commanded to follow them absolutely. This impossibility proves their protection from sin. The passage also clarifies exceptions for acts specific to the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the core proof
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the key premise: if messengers betrayed by committing a forbidden or disliked act, that act would turn into obedience for us because of the command to follow them. This is impossible, so messengers cannot betray.
Notice the logical structure: if P (betrayal) then Q (turns into obedience); Q is impossible, therefore not-P.
2
Consider the exception
Read the part about exceptions. Some acts are specific to the Prophet (e.g., marrying more than four). These are not general obligations. The passage clarifies that unless an act is proven to be a special prerogative, we must follow it without hesitation.
This prevents the argument from being misapplied to unique prophetic privileges.
3
Reflect on the consensus
Note the final point: the Companions unanimously followed the Prophet in all statements and actions without hesitation. This consensus supports the absolute nature of following and confirms that nothing he did can be sinful or even disliked.
The consensus is a historical support for the rational proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
برهان وجوب الأمانة للرسل عليهم السلام لو خانوا بفعل محرّم أو مكروه لا نقلب المحرّم أو المكروه طاعة في حقهم. لأن الله قد أمرنا معشر العباد بالاقتداء بهم في أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، قال تعالى في حق نبينا : ( قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْبِبْكُمُ اللهُ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ وَاللهُ ) (۱) وتقريراتهم وسكوتهم على الفعل إذ لا يقرّون على خطأ ، ويستثنى من ذلك ما ثبتت خصوصيته بهم كنكاح ما زاد على الأربع. ويعلم من ذلك أنه ليس للمكلف منا أن يتوقف في فعل شيء مما ثبت عنه ، لاحتمال الخصوصية ، بل يتبعه في جميع أقواله وأفعاله إلا ما ثبت أنه من خصوصياته لإطلاق قولـه تعالى قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِى ) وقد أجمعت الصحابة على اتباعه عليه الصلاة والسلام في أقواله وأفعاله من غير توقف
Proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for the messengers, peace be upon them: If they were to betray by committing a forbidden or disliked act, then the forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience in their right. Because Allah has commanded us, the servants, to follow them in their statements and actions. He said, the Exalted, regarding our Prophet: 'Say, if you love Allah, then follow me, Allah will love you and forgive you your sins. And Allah is...' (1) And their approvals and silences upon an action, since they do not approve of error. And excepted from that is what has been established as specific to them, like marrying more than four. And it is understood from that that it is not for the morally obligated person among us to hesitate in doing anything that has been established from him, due to the possibility of specificity; rather, he follows him in all his statements and actions except what has been established as his special characteristics, because of the absolute nature of His statement, the Exalted: 'Say, if you love Allah, then follow me.' And the Companions unanimously agreed upon following him, peace be upon him, in his statements and actions without hesitation.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage provides a rational proof for the obligatory trustworthiness (amanah) of messengers. The argument is: if a messenger were to commit a forbidden or disliked action, that action would, by virtue of the command to follow them, become an act of obedience for us. But this is impossible because Allah commands us to follow them absolutely. Therefore, messengers cannot commit any forbidden or disliked act. The author then discusses exceptions (such as marrying more than four, a privilege exclusive to the Prophet). He concludes that a believer must not hesitate to follow anything established from the Prophet, unless it is proven to be a special prerogative. The Companions' consensus on following without hesitation supports this.

Key Terms
أمانة
رسل
اقتداء
خصوصية
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The possibility of prophetic specificities allows doubt about whether we must follow all of the Prophet's actions.
Correction: The author clarifies that we must follow everything unless it is proven to be a special characteristic; the default is absolute following.

Checkpoint

A) It would remain disliked
B) It would become obedience for us
C) It would become forbidden
D) It would be cancelled

Key Takeaway
Messengers are trustworthy because any sin from them would become obligatory for us, which is impossible given the absolute command to follow them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that any sin from the Prophet would become obedience for us. The Logical Proof for Prophetic Trustworthiness
Sanusi presents a logical proof for prophetic trustworthiness using the impossibility of forbidden acts becoming obedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that prophets must be trustworthy (infallible) based on the impossibility of a forbidden act becoming an act of obedience.

Core Idea
If prophets could sin, following them would mean obeying sin—an impossibility.

Sanusi now establishes a crucial attribute of prophets: trustworthiness (amana). He does so by a tight logical argument, not just by citing scripture. The proof shows that if prophets could commit forbidden acts, those acts would have to be considered obedience for them—because Allah commands us to follow them. But Allah never commands what is forbidden. Therefore, prophets cannot commit forbidden acts. This lesson walks through that argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get its rhythm, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: conditional statement, evidence from Quran and hadith, logical conclusion.
The proof uses a conditional: 'if they betrayed... then the forbidden would become obedience.'
2
Identify the key premises
Find the two main premises: (1) Allah commands us to follow the prophets in all their actions. (2) Allah does not command what is forbidden or disliked.
These premises are supported by Quranic verses.
3
Understand the contradiction
If a prophet committed a forbidden act, then that act would be an act of obedience for us (because we must follow it). But it cannot be both forbidden and obedience. This is a logical contradiction.
Sanusi calls it 'conjunction of two contradictories' (جمع النقيضين).
4
Follow the conclusion
Since the contradiction is impossible, the initial assumption (that prophets could commit forbidden acts) is false. Therefore, prophets are trustworthy—they do not betray.
The proof covers both forbidden and disliked acts, establishing complete infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
برهان وجوب الأمانة للرسل عليهم السلام
لو خانوا بفعل محرّم أو مكروه لا نقلب المحرّم أو المكروه طاعة في حقهم.
لأن الله قد أمرنا معشر العباد بالاقتداء بهم في أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، قال تعالى في حق نبينا : ( قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْبِبْكُمُ اللهُ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ وَاللهُ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ ) [آل عمران : ۳۱]، وقال تعالى ( وَاتَّبِعُوهُ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَهْتَدُونَ ) (الأعراف : ١٥٨) ، وقال عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين المهديين. والله تعالى لا يأمر بمحرم ولا مكروه لقوله تعالى ( قُلْ إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَأْمُرُ بِالْفَحْشَاءِ ) [الأعراف: ۲۸]، وانقلاب المحرم أو المكروه طاعة في حقهم محال لأنه جمع بين النقيضين، فإذا بطل انقلاب المحرّم أو المكروه طاعة في حقهم بطل صدور الخيانة منهم، وإذا بطل صدور الخيانة منهم وجب لهم الأمانة وهو المطلوب.
Proof of the necessity of trustworthiness for the messengers, peace be upon them: If they were to betray by committing a forbidden (muharram) or disliked (makruh) act, then the forbidden or disliked would become obedience (ta'a) in their right. Because Allah has commanded us, the community of servants, to follow them in their statements and actions. He said, exalted, regarding our Prophet: 'Say: If you love Allah, then follow me, Allah will love you and forgive you your sins, and Allah is Forgiving, Merciful' [Al 'Imran: 31]. And He said: 'And follow him that you may be guided' [Al-A'raf: 158]. And he (the Prophet) said: 'Hold fast to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs.' And Allah, exalted, does not command what is forbidden or disliked, for His saying: 'Say: Indeed, Allah does not command immorality' [Al-A'raf: 28]. And the transformation of the forbidden or disliked into obedience in their right is impossible because it is the conjunction of two contradictories. Since the transformation of the forbidden or disliked into obedience in their right is invalid, then the occurrence of betrayal from them is invalid. And since the occurrence of betrayal from them is invalid, trustworthiness is necessary for them – and that is what was sought.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof (burhan) for the necessity of trustworthiness (amana) in prophets. The proof is structured as a conditional argument: if prophets were to commit a forbidden or disliked act, then that act would have to become an act of obedience for them, because Allah commands us to follow them in all their actions. If we are commanded to follow them, then whatever they do becomes a model for us. However, Allah does not command what is forbidden or disliked. Therefore, the act cannot be forbidden or disliked for them; it must be permissible or obligatory. But if they committed a forbidden act, it would have to be considered obedience for them, which is contradictory because an act cannot be both forbidden and obedience simultaneously (this is the conjunction of two contradictories). Therefore, it is impossible for prophets to commit forbidden or disliked acts. Hence, they are trustworthy (ma'sum) from such acts. The proof cites Quranic verses commanding us to follow the Prophet, and a hadith urging adherence to his sunnah. It also cites the verse 'Allah does not command immorality' to establish that Allah only commands good. The key step is that if prophets could sin, we would be commanded to follow sin, which is impossible. The proof concludes that trustworthiness (i.e., infallibility) is necessary for them.

Key Terms
الأمانة (trustworthiness)
الخيانة (betrayal)
المحرّم (forbidden)
المكروه (disliked)
الطاعة (obedience)
جمع النقيضين (conjunction of contradictories)
الاقتداء (following)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof only covers major sins, not minor sins or disliked acts.
Correction: The proof explicitly includes both forbidden (muharram) and disliked (makruh) acts, establishing complete infallibility from all sin, minor or major.

Checkpoint
What is the central logical impossibility that this proof relies on?
A) The conjunction of two contradictories (جمع النقيضين)
B) The impossibility of Allah commanding evil
C) The Qur'an being abrogated
D) The prophets lying about revelation

Key Takeaway
Prophets cannot commit any forbidden or disliked act because if they did, that act would have to be both forbidden and obedience—a logical contradiction—so trustworthiness is necessarily part of their character.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly follow the Prophet in all your statements and actions, or do you selectively follow only what is convenient? Reflect on one area of your life where you excuse yourself from the sunnah, and commit to changing it starting today.
?
The proof shows that a prophet cannot even commit a disliked act. Yet how often do you downplay your own minor sins or disliked habits as 'harmless'? What does this reveal about your reverence for the Prophet's perfect example?
?
If you genuinely believed that following the Prophet in every detail is the path to Allah's love and forgiveness, would you change anything in your daily routine? Name one specific change you will make this week.

The Obligation to Follow the Prophet and the Exception of Specificity
The author explains the rule of following the Prophet and the exception of his specific prerogatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's tacit approvals and silences are binding, and that the only exception is matters proven to be specific to him.

Core Idea
Follow the Prophet in all things unless proven specific to him.

This passage establishes the foundational principle that the Prophet's actions and approvals are authoritative. It clarifies that we are not to hesitate in following him due to the possibility that an action might be specific to him, but rather we follow unless the specificity is proven. This is based on the Qur'anic command to follow the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Notice the structure: first tacit approvals, then the exception, then the general rule.
The passage is dense; read it twice.
2
Identify the exception
Find the exception to the general rule of following. What specific matter is mentioned as being exclusive to the Prophet? How does it relate to the general obligation?
Marriage of more than four is given as an example.
3
Understand the reasoning
The passage argues that the possibility of specificity does not justify hesitation. Why is that? Trace the logic: the Qur'anic command is general, so any exception must be proven.
This reinforces the principle of following without delay.

رضي الله عنه، إبليس أنهم قتلوه، فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا نبرح حتى نناجزهم الحرب، ودعا الناس عند الشجرة للبيعة على الموت أو على أن لا يفروا فبايعوه على ذلك، فلما سمع الكفار بالمبايعة نزل بهم الخوف وأرسلوا رجلاً منهم يعتذر بأن القتال لم يقع إلا من سفهائهم، وطلب أن يرسل من أسر منهم فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: إني غير مرسل حتى ترسلوا أصحابي، فقال ذلك الرجل: أنصفتنا. فبعث إليهم فأرسلوا عثمان وجماعة من المسلمين، ووقع الصلح بينه وبين ذلك الرجل على شرط أن يوضع الحرب بينهم عشر سنين، وأن يَوْمَن بعضهم بعضاً، وأن يرجع عنهم عامهم ويأتي معتمراً في العام القابل، وأن يردَّ إليهم من مسلماً، وأن لا يردّوا إليه من جاء إليهم ممن تبعهم، وكتب لهم علي بن أبي طالب بذلك كتاباً، فكره المسلمون هذه الشروط، وقالوا يا رسول الله إنا نردّ ولا يردّون، قال: نعم أما من ذهب منا إليهم فأبعده الله تعالى، ومن جاء منهم إلينا فسيجعل الله له فرجاً ومخرجاً، ثم قال لأصحابه: قوموا فانحروا واحلقوا، قال الراوي: فوالله ما قام منهم أحد حتى قال ذلك ثلاثاً. فلما لم يفعلوا دخل على أم سلمة وقال: هلك المسلمون أمرتهم أن بعضاً كما في البخاري.
And their approvals and silences regarding an action, for they do not approve of error. And from that is excepted what is established as specific to them, such as marriage of more than four. And from that it is known that it is not for the responsible person among us to hesitate in anything established from him, due to the possibility of specificity; rather he follows him in all his statements and actions except what is established as being among his specificities, because of the generality of His saying: 'Say: If you love Allah, then follow me.' And the Companions were unanimous on following him, peace and blessings be upon him, in his statements and actions without hesitation. But this is with regard to the general case; otherwise, hesitation did occur from them in the Conquest of Mecca, when the Prophet ordered them to break their fast in Ramadan, but they persisted in abstaining; then he took a cup and drank, so they drank. And in the Battle of Hudaybiyyah, when Allah... and he ordered them to slaughter [their sacrificial animals] and shave [their heads], but they did not do so, because they were absorbed in reflecting on the hardship that had occurred. That is because when he and his Companions had set out for 'Umrah and camped at the far end of Hudaybiyyah, the polytheists prevented them from entering Mecca. So he sent 'Uthman ibn 'Affan with a letter to the leaders of Mecca informing them that he had only come as a pilgrim, not as a fighter. They insisted that he should not enter Mecca this year. Then a man from one party threw at the other party, so there was a battle between them with arrows and stones. The Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, restrained some of them, and they detained 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, may Allah be pleased with him. And Satan spread the news that they had killed him. So the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'We will not leave until we engage them in war.' He called the people to the tree for a pledge of allegiance to die or not to flee, and they pledged allegiance to him on that. When the disbelievers heard of the pledge, fear fell upon them, and they sent a man from among them apologizing that the fighting had only occurred from their foolish ones, and he asked that those captured from them be sent. The Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'I will not send anyone until you send my Companions.' That man said: 'You have been fair to us.' So he sent to them, and they sent 'Uthman and a group of Muslims. And a truce was made between him and that man on the condition that war would be set aside between them for ten years, that they would give security to one another, that he would return from them that year and come for 'Umrah the following year, that they would return to them anyone who came to them as a Muslim, and that they would not return to him anyone who came to them from among those who followed them. 'Ali ibn Abi Talib wrote that document for them. The Muslims disliked these conditions and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, we return [people to them] and they do not return [to us]?' He said: 'Yes. As for those who go from us to them, Allah has distanced them; and as for those who come from them to us, Allah will grant them relief and a way out.' Then he said to his Companions: 'Arise and slaughter [your animals] and shave [your heads].' The narrator said: 'By Allah, not one of them stood up until he said it three times. When they did not do it, he entered upon Umm Salamah and said: 'The Muslims are destroyed! I commanded them to shave and slaughter, but they did not do it.' She said: 'O Messenger of Allah, do not blame them, for this truce was hard upon them. Go out and do not speak to anyone until you have done that.' So he went out and slaughtered with his own hand and called his barber. When they saw that, they arose and slaughtered, and some of them began to shave others... as in al-Bukhari.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory note on the ruling of following the Prophet. It begins by stating that the Prophet's tacit approvals and silences regarding actions are also binding, because he does not approve of error. An exception is made for matters that are specifically for him, like marrying more than four. From this, it is understood that a believer should not hesitate to follow any action established from the Prophet, because the possibility that it might be specific to him is not a valid reason for hesitation; rather one follows him in all statements and actions unless it is proven to be a specific prerogative. This is based on the general command in the verse 'Say: If you love Allah, then follow me.' The Companions were unanimous in following him without hesitation in general, but there were instances of hesitation due to hardship. Two examples are given: at the Conquest of Mecca (when ordered to break fast in Ramadan, they hesitated until the Prophet himself drank), and at Hudaybiyyah (when ordered to sacrifice and shave, they hesitated due to the perceived humiliation of the truce). The passage then narrates the full story of Hudaybiyyah to illustrate how the Prophet eventually resolved the hesitation by performing the action himself, leading the Companions to follow immediately. This demonstrates that the obligation to follow is absolute, and even when the command feels difficult, the Prophet's own action removes any excuse for delay. The story also highlights the virtues of the Companions and the wisdom of the Prophet in handling the situation.

Key Terms
التقريرات (tacit approvals)
السكوت (silence)
الخصوصية (specificity)
الاقتداء (following)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if an action might be specific to the Prophet, it is permissible to hesitate or not follow.
Correction: The passage clarifies that hesitation is not allowed; one must follow unless specificity is proven.

Checkpoint
What is the exception to following the Prophet in all actions?
A) Actions that are difficult
B) Actions proven specific to the Prophet
C) Actions that contradict the Quran
D) Actions that bring hardship

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's actions and approvals are authoritative unless proven specific to him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the verse 'If you love Allah, then follow me,' do you feel a genuine urgency to examine your daily choices against the Prophet's example, or have you become comfortable with selective obedience? What is one specific sunnah you have delayed or ignored while convincing yourself it might be 'just for him'?
?
The Prophet's silence on certain actions is considered approval. Are there actions in your life—habits, words, or dealings—that you know would have troubled him had he witnessed them? Why do you continue them despite knowing he would not approve?
?
The lesson warns against hesitating to follow due to the possibility of specificity. Is your hesitation rooted in love and caution, or in convenience and laziness? What would it cost you to follow the Prophet in one area you have been avoiding?

The Hudaybiyyah Story: Obedience Without Hesitation
The author narrates the story of Hudaybiyyah to illustrate how the Companions' hesitation was overcome by the Prophet's own action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet resolved the Companions' hesitation at Hudaybiyyah, demonstrating that obedience must be immediate even when the command seems difficult.

Core Idea
When the Prophet commands, obedience should not be delayed even in hardship.

After establishing the general obligation to follow the Prophet, the commentator provides two examples where the Companions hesitated due to hardship. The most detailed is the story of Hudaybiyyah, where the Companions initially failed to obey the order to sacrifice and shave. The Prophet's decisive action—doing it himself—immediately corrected the hesitancy, highlighting the principle that obedience to the Prophet is required without delay.

Guided Path
1
Read the Hudaybiyyah story
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Pay attention to the flow of events: the expedition, the blockade, the negotiations, the truce, and the final command.
This is a long narrative; take your time.
2
Identify the hesitation
Why did the Companions hesitate when the Prophet ordered them to slaughter and shave? What was their emotional state?
They were distressed by the truce terms.
3
Notice the Prophet's response
How did the Prophet react to their hesitation? What did he do after consulting Umm Salamah?
He performed the actions himself without speaking.
4
Reflect on the lesson
What does this story teach about the obligation to obey the Prophet? Why did the Companions follow immediately after seeing his action?
The Prophet's example removed all doubt.

The Companions were unanimous in following him without hesitation in general, but there were instances of hesitation due to hardship. Two examples are given: at the Conquest of Mecca (when ordered to break fast in Ramadan, they hesitated until the Prophet himself drank), and at Hudaybiyyah (when ordered to sacrifice and shave, they hesitated due to the perceived humiliation of the truce). The passage then narrates the full story of Hudaybiyyah to illustrate how the Prophet eventually resolved the hesitation by performing the action himself, leading the Companions to follow immediately. This demonstrates that the obligation to follow is absolute, and even when the command feels difficult, the Prophet's own action removes any excuse for delay. The story also highlights the virtues of the Companions and the wisdom of the Prophet in handling the situation.

Key Terms
الحديبية (Hudaybiyyah)
البيعة (pledge of allegiance)
الصلح (truce)
النحر (slaughter)
الحلق (shaving)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that hesitation is permissible when a command seems unreasonable or difficult.
Correction: The passage shows that hesitation was corrected immediately by the Prophet's action, emphasizing that obedience is required regardless of personal feelings.

Checkpoint
How did the Prophet respond when the Companions did not obey his command to slaughter and shave at Hudaybiyyah?
A) He reprimanded them harshly
B) He performed the act himself
C) He repeated the command seven times
D) He cancelled the command

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's own action at Hudaybiyyah teaches that obedience should not be delayed by hardship; the leader's example inspires compliance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When has a clear command from Allah felt so hard that you hesitated to obey it? What was the real reason for that hesitation, and what did it cost you?
?
The Companions needed the Prophet to act first before they could obey. What command from Allah are you waiting for a sign or example before you act? Why can't you act on it right now?
?
Umm Salamah advised the Prophet to lead by action rather than words. Who in your life is waiting for you to take the first step in obedience, even while they wrestle with their own doubts?

Proof of Human Attributes in Prophets
Sanusi proves the permissibility of human attributes in prophets with rational and scriptural evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi proves that human attributes in prophets are rationally permissible and supported by revelation and consensus.

Core Idea
Prophets had human attributes; their occurrence proves permissibility.

This lesson presents Sanusi's proof that prophets possessed ordinary human traits like eating and walking. He first defines permissible attributes, then gives a rational argument based on observed occurrence, and finally confirms it with Quran, hadith, and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Note the structure: definition, rational proof, conditional logic, and scriptural support.
2
Identify the rational proof
Find the sentence 'The proof of their permissibility is their occurrence to them.' Understand that direct observation or mutawatir reports establish occurrence.
3
Understand the conditional argument
Trace the logical chain: denying occurrence is false → impermissibility is false → permissibility is true. This is the core rational demonstration.
4
Review the scriptural evidence
Look at the Quran verses (al-Furqan 17, 20) and the hadith about the Prophet's human actions. Note the mention of consensus.
5
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to solidify the rational proof. Then consider the misconception about prophets being free of all human attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
برهان جواز الأعراض البشرية على الرسل عليهم السلام والأعراض الجائزة هي التي لا تؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العلية ودليل جوازها هو وقوعها بهم. فمن كان في عصرهم رآها ومن لم يكن في عصرهم فقد ورده الخبر المتواتر بهذا الأمر. والحاصل أن الأعراض البشرية شوهد وقوعها بهم تارة وعدم وقوعها بهم تارة أخرى وما كان بهذا السبيل فهو الجائز. فإذا بطل نفي وقوع الأعراض البشرية بهم بطل عدم جوازها وإذا بطل عدم جوازها وجب أن تكون الأعراض جائزة في حقهم وهو المطلوب. وقد دل الكتاب والسنة والإجماع على ذلك، قال تعالى ( وَقَالُواْ مَالِ هَذَا ﴿ الرَّسُولِ يَأْكُلُ الطَّعَامَ وَيَمْشِي فِي الْأَسْوَاقِ ﴾ (الفرقان : ۱۷، وقال تعالى ( وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا قَبْلَكَ مِنَ الْمُرْسَلِينَ إِلَّا إِنَّهُمْ لَيَأْكُلُونَ الطَّعَامَ وَيَمْشُونَ فِي الْأَسْوَاقِ ) الفرقان : ۱۲۰. وأما السنة فقد صح أنه لا لو أكل وشرب ونام وتزوج وطلق وباع واشترى وكذا غيره من الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، وقال له أما والله إني لأخشاكم لله وأتقاكم له لكني أصوم وأفطر وأصلي وأرقد وأتزوج النساء فمن رغب عن سنتي فليس مني (١) وقد أجمعت الأمة على ذلك.
Proof of the permissibility of human attributes in the messengers, peace be upon them. The permissible attributes are those that do not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks. The proof of their permissibility is their occurrence to them. So whoever was in their time saw them, and whoever was not in their time, the mutawatir report has reached him about this. The summary is that human attributes were observed occurring to them sometimes and not occurring to them at other times, and whatever is like this is permissible. So if the denial of the occurrence of human attributes to them is invalidated, then the impermissibility of their occurrence is invalidated, and if the impermissibility is invalidated, then the attributes must be permissible in their regard, which is the desired conclusion. The Book, the Sunnah, and consensus indicate that. Allah says: 'And they say, What is wrong with this Messenger that he eats food and walks in the markets?' (Al-Furqan: 17) And He says: 'And We sent not before you any of the messengers except that they ate food and walked in the markets' (Al-Furqan: 20). As for the Sunnah, it is established that he ate, drank, slept, married, divorced, bought, and sold, and likewise other prophets, peace be upon them. And he said: 'By Allah, I am the most fearful of Allah among you and the most pious, but I fast and break fast, pray and sleep, and marry women; so whoever turns away from my Sunnah is not of me.' And the nation has unanimously agreed upon that.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the permissibility of human attributes (a'rad bashariyya) in prophets. The author begins by defining permissible human attributes as those that do not detract from the prophets' high station. He then presents the rational proof: these attributes are permissible because they are observed to occur to them. Some people witnessed them directly, and others received mutawatir reports. The argument uses a conditional structure: if the denial of their occurrence is invalid, then the claim of their impermissibility is invalid, and consequently they are permissible. This is the logical demonstration. Then he supports it with scriptural evidence: Quranic verses stating that prophets eat and walk in markets, and a hadith where the Prophet says he fasts and breaks fast, etc., and mentions the consensus of the ummah.

Key Terms
الأعراض البشرية
جواز
الرسل
الخبر المتواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophets must be free from all human attributes.
Correction: Only those attributes that cause deficiency in their ranks are impossible; ordinary human attributes are permissible and actually occurred.

Checkpoint
What is the primary rational evidence for the permissibility of human attributes in prophets?
A) Scriptural texts
B) Consensus of the ummah
C) Their actual occurrence to prophets
D) Their necessity for legislation

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of human attributes in prophets is proven by their actual occurrence, supported by revelation and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of the Prophet’s humanity—his eating, walking, marrying—does it make him seem closer to you or less awe-inspiring? Have you ever subconsciously wished he were more superhuman to avoid confronting your own weaknesses? What would it take for you to see his humanity as a model for your own worship, not a concession?
?
The proof of permissibility rests on what was actually observed. Look at your own life: if someone observed your actions, would they see evidence of your beliefs, or would they see a disconnect? Where are you hiding behind theoretical faith without letting it manifest in tangible, human acts of worship?
?
Sanusi argues that prophets’ human attributes are permissible because they occurred without causing deficiency. What human attributes in your own life—your desires, your routines, your struggles—are you using as excuses to lower your spiritual rank? Are you willing to transform them into acts of devotion, just as the Prophet did with his eating, sleeping, and marriage?

Benefits of Human Attributes in Prophets: Magnification of Rewards and Legislation
Sanusi enumerates two benefits of prophets' afflictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two primary benefits of prophets experiencing human afflictions: magnification of their rewards and the establishment of legal rulings for the community.

Core Idea
Prophets' afflictions are not deficiencies but means for reward multiplication and teaching.

Sanusi begins by stating two benefits of human attributes in prophets. First, these experiences multiply their rewards because of their patience. Second, they serve as a source of legislation, teaching the community how to act in similar situations. This lesson explores these benefits, supported by a hadith and scholarly commentary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the full translation. Notice the two distinct benefits Sanusi presents.
The passage uses concise language; the commentary will clarify.
2
Identify the two benefits
Find where Sanusi introduces 'Magnification of rewards' and 'Legislation'. Understand how each is defined.
The first benefit is explained with a hadith about prophets being multiplied in pain.
3
Reflect on the hadith and commentary
Consider the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Imam al-Qushayri's statement about affliction being for the awliya. How do these support the benefits?
The hadith shows the Prophet's own affliction and the promise of multiplied reward.

فوائد وقوع الأعراض بهم عليهم السلام تعظيم الأجور أي تكثير الثواب باعتبار ما يطرأ على ظواهرهم من الآفات والتغيرات والآلام وتجرع كأس الحمام فقد مرض الله واشتكى وأصابه الحر والبرد والجوع والعطش وأصاب غيره من الأنبياء ما هو أعظم من ذلك. فكل هذه الأعراض تقع ويصبرون عليها، فهم أشد الناس بلاء. قال : 'إنا كذلك معشر الأنبياء يضاعف علينا الوجع ليضاعف لنا الأجر'. وهذه الأعراض حظها منهم الظاهر وأما بواطنهم فمنزهة عن ذلك. وقد حفظت من النوم الذي هو أدنى فما بالك بغيره. التشريع : أي التعليم للغير كما عرفنا أحكام الصلاة من السهو الواقع له عليه الصلاة والسلام، وعرفنا كيف تؤدى الصلاة في المرض من فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام. (۱) رواه ابن أبي الدنيا في كتاب المرض والكفارات عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال : 'دخلت على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو محموم فوضعت يدي فوق القطيفة فوجدت حرارة الحمى فقلت : ما أشد حماك يا رسول الله ! قال : إنا كذلك معشر الأنبياء يضاعف علينا الوجع ليضاعف لنا الأجر ، قلت : يا رسول الله فأي الناس أشد بلاء؟ قال : الأنبياء قلت : ثم من قال : ثم الصالحون إن كان ليبتلى بالفقر حتى ما يجد إلا العباءة فيجوبها ويلبسها وإن كان أحدهم ليبتلى بالقمل حتى يقتله القمل وكان ذلك أحب إليهم من العطاء'. ورواه الحاكم في المستدرك عن عطاء بن يسار عن أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله تعالى عنه قال : 'دخلت على النبي وهو محموم فوضعت يدي من فوق القطيفة فوجدت حرارة الحمى فقلت : ما أشد حماك يا رسول الله ! قال : إنا كذلك معشر الأنبياء يضاعف علينا الوجع ليضاعف لنا الأجر قال : فقلت : يا رسول الله أي الناس أشد بلاء؟ قال : الأنبياء قلت : ثم من؟ قال : ثم الصالحون إن كان الرجل ليبتلى بالفقر حتى ما يجد إلا العباء فيحويها ويلبسها وإن كان أحدهم ليبتلى بالقمل حتى يقتله القمل وكان ذلك أحب إليهم من العطاء إليكم' هذا حديث صحيح على شرط مسلم ولم يخرجاه.(س). قال الإمام القشيري : ليس كل أحد أهلاً للبلاء إذ البلاء للأولياء، وأما الأجانب فيتجاوز عنهم ويخلي سبيلهم، وروي أنه أراد أن يتزوج بامرأة فقيل له : إنها لم تمرض فأعرض عنها، وحكي أن عمار بن ياسر تزوج امرأة لم تمرض فطلقها. (ج) واعلم أن عروض هذه المشاق للأنبياء والأولياء يناسب وظيفتهم التي كلفهم الله تعالى بها، وقاموا هم بحقها، فإن هذه الأمور لا بد أن تلاقي المناكدة من عامة الناس. مما يترتب على الصبر على ذلك عظيم الثواب وهكذا شأن كل من تصدى للقيام بهذه الوظيفة، فإنها عظيمة الخطر بالغة التأثير وما كان هذا شأنه فلا بد أن يوجد من يعارضه يقاوم الداعي إليه ، فتنبه (س).
Benefits of the occurrence of human attributes to them, peace be upon them. Magnification of rewards, i.e., multiplication of recompense, considering what befalls their outer forms of afflictions, changes, pains, and swallowing the cup of death. For Allah (the Prophet) became ill, complained, was affected by heat, cold, hunger, and thirst, and other prophets were afflicted with what is greater than that. So all these attributes occur and they patiently endure them, so they are the most severely tested of people. He said: 'Indeed, we, the company of prophets, are multiplied in pain so that our reward is multiplied.' These attributes affect only their outward; as for their inner selves, they are free from that. And they were protected from sleep, which is the least, so what about other things? Legislation: i.e., teaching others, as we learned the rulings of prayer from the forgetfulness that occurred to him, peace be upon him, and we learned how to pray during illness from his action, peace be upon him. (1) Narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in the book of illness and expiations from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: 'I entered upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was feverish, and I placed my hand over the cover and found the heat of the fever, and I said: How intense is your fever, O Messenger of Allah! He said: Indeed, we, the company of prophets, are multiplied in pain so that our reward is multiplied. I said: O Messenger of Allah, which people are most severely tested? He said: The prophets. I said: Then who? He said: Then the righteous. Indeed, one of them may be tried with poverty until he finds only a cloak, so he sews it and wears it, and one of them may be tried with lice until the lice kill him, and that was more beloved to them than gifts.' And al-Hakim narrated it in al-Mustadrak via 'Ata' ibn Yasar from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'I entered upon the Prophet while he was feverish, and I placed my hand from above the cover and found the heat of the fever, and I said: How intense is your fever, O Messenger of Allah! He said: Indeed, we, the company of prophets, are multiplied in pain so that our reward is multiplied. He said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, which people are most severely tested? He said: The prophets. I said: Then who? He said: Then the righteous. Indeed, a man may be tried with poverty until he finds only a cloak, so he wraps it and wears it, and one of them may be tried with lice until the lice kill him, and that was more beloved to them than giving to you.' This is a sahih hadith according to the condition of Muslim, but they did not record it. (s). Imam al-Qushayri said: Not everyone is worthy of affliction, for affliction is for the awliya; as for others, they are overlooked and left alone. And it is reported that he wanted to marry a woman and was told she had never been ill, so he turned away from her. And it is narrated that 'Ammar ibn Yasir married a woman who had never been ill and divorced her. (j) And know that the occurrence of these hardships to the prophets and awliya is appropriate for their function that Allah entrusted them with, and they fulfilled it properly, for these matters must encounter opposition from ordinary people. This results in great reward for patience. Likewise, whoever undertakes this function, it is of great significance and powerful effect, and such a matter must have opponents who resist its call, so be alert. (s).
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage explains the benefits of human attributes in prophets. Two benefits are highlighted: (1) Magnification of rewards: the prophets endure hardships, and their patience multiplies their reward. (2) Legislation: the prophets' actions in these states provide guidance for the ummah, such as rulings on prayer during illness and forgetfulness in prayer. The text then provides a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri describing the Prophet's fever and his statement about prophets being multiplied in pain for multiplied reward. It also includes commentary from Imam al-Qushayri on the nature of affliction, that it is for the awliya, and notes that the prophets' inner selves are protected from these attributes. The passage concludes with a reminder that the afflictions are appropriate for their function and that patience yields great reward.

Benefits of Afflictions on Prophets and Their Reward
Sanusi explains that prophets' outward afflictions multiply reward while their inner selves are immune.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets experience outward afflictions and how this multiplies their reward while their inner purity remains untouched.

Core Idea
Prophets' outward suffering multiplies reward; their inner selves are immune.

This lesson explores a profound aspect of prophethood: the purpose of afflictions that befall prophets outwardly. Sanusi explains that these afflictions are not signs of imperfection but means of multiplying divine reward. Moreover, he emphasizes that prophets' inner beings are completely protected from any deficiency. Understanding this clarifies the unique station of prophets and guards against misconceptions about their suffering.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the precise wording: 'تعظيم الأجور' and 'فهم أشد الناس بلاء'.
2
Identify the two key claims
The passage makes two main claims: (1) outward afflictions multiply reward, and (2) prophets' inner selves are immune from these afflictions. Find the sentences that state these.
3
Reflect on the hadith
The passage quotes a hadith: 'Indeed we, the company of prophets, are multiplied in pain so that the reward is multiplied for us.' Ask yourself: How does this hadith support the first claim?
This hadith directly ties outward pain to multiplied reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوائد وقوع الأعراض بهم عليهم السلام تعظيم الأجور أي تكثير الثواب باعتبار ما يطرأ على ظواهرهم من الآفات والتغيرات والآلام وتجرع كأس الحمام فقد مرض الله واشتكى وأصابه الحر والبرد والجوع والعطش وأصاب غيره من الأنبياء ما هو أعظم من ذلك. فكل هذه الأعراض تقع ويصبرون عليها، فهم أشد الناس بلاء. قال : " إنا كذلك معشر الأنبياء يضاعف علينا الوجع ليضاعف لنا الأجر ) . وهذه الأعراض حظها منهم الظاهر وأما بواطنهم فمنزهة عن ذلك. وقد حفظت من النوم الذي هو أدنى فما بالك بغيره.
Benefits of the occurrence of accidents upon them, peace be upon them: magnification of rewards, meaning multiplication of recompense in consideration of what befalls their outward appearances of afflictions, changes, pains, and the swallowing of the cup of death. For Allah became ill and complained, and heat, cold, hunger, and thirst afflicted him, and other prophets were afflicted with what is greater than that. So all these accidents occur and they are patient upon them, thus they are the most severely tried of people. He said: 'Indeed, we, the company of prophets, are multiplied in pain so that the reward is multiplied for us.' And these accidents have their share from them outwardly, but their inner selves are immune from that. And they were protected from sleep, which is the lowest, so what about other than it?
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the benefits of afflictions (a'rad) that befall prophets. It begins by stating that the purpose of these afflictions is to multiply reward (ta'zim al-ujur). The author then lists examples of afflictions that prophets endure: illness, pain, heat, cold, hunger, thirst, and even the bitterness of death. The text mentions that other prophets faced even greater trials. It affirms that prophets undergo these outward trials and bear them patiently, making them the most severely tested of people. A hadith is cited from the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating that pain is multiplied for prophets so that reward is multiplied. The author then clarifies a crucial theological point: these afflictions only affect the outward (zahir) of the prophets; their inner selves (bawatin) are immune and protected from any deficiency. The passage concludes by noting that even sleep—considered the lowest form of human state—is protected from them, implying that all other forms of imperfection are even more impossible for them. This guards against the misunderstanding that prophets suffer spiritually or that affliction implies divine displeasure.

Correction: The passage clarifies that afflictions only affect outward appearances to multiply reward; their inner selves are immune and protected from any deficiency.

Key Takeaway
Prophets endure outward hardships to earn multiplied rewards, while their inner purity remains untouched.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson shows that prophets' inner selves are pure and immune from deficiency. But your heart is not immune—what impurities (like pride, envy, or heedlessness) have you allowed to take root while you focus only on outward hardships? What specific steps will you take this week to purify your inner state?
?
Even sleep, the lowest form of human state, is protected from prophets. You are not protected from such deficiencies. How does this awareness deepen your reliance on Allah to guard your heart? What practical changes will you make to seek His protection over your inner self?

The Wisdom of Trials for Prophets and Saints
Sanusi cites and comments on hadith about prophets' trials.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets and saints endure the greatest trials and how this relates to their high station and function.

Core Idea
Trials are a sign of closeness, not displeasure, for the righteous.

Sanusi presents a powerful hadith that turns our common perception of trials upside down. Rather than indicating divine anger, severe trials are a privilege granted to prophets and saints, leading to multiplied reward. This lesson unpacks the hadith and the accompanying commentary to reveal the profound wisdom behind tribulation.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narration
Read the Arabic text and translation of the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. Notice the Prophet's own fever and his explanation that prophets have their pain multiplied for multiplied reward.
This hadith is authentic according to Muslim's criteria but not in Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Identify the most severely tried
The Prophet clearly states that prophets are the most severely tried, then the righteous. Reflect on the implications.
3
Examine al-Qushayri's commentary
Read al-Qushayri's statement that not everyone is worthy of trial—it is for the awliya. Consider the anecdote about turning away from a woman who never fell ill.
4
Understand the function-based explanation
The author explains that hardships befit the function of prophets and saints because their mission faces opposition. Patience yields great reward.
This is a key insight: trials are inherent to the role.
5
Apply the lesson personally
Reflect on how this perspective changes your view of personal trials. What can you learn from the example of the righteous preferring trials over worldly gifts?
This is about internalizing the wisdom.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) رواه ابن أبي الدنيا في كتاب المرض والكفارات عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال : " دخلت على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو محموم فوضعت يدي فوق القطيفة فوجدت حرارة الحمى فقلت : ما أشد حماك يا رسول الله ! قال : إنا كذلك معشر الأنبياء يضاعف علينا الوجع ليضاعف لنا الأجر ، قلت : يا رسول الله فأي الناس أشد بلاء؟ قال : الأنبياء قلت : ثم من قال : ثم الصالحون إن كان ليبتلى بالفقر حتى ما يجد إلا العباءة فيجوبها ويلبسها وإن كان أحدهم ليبتلى بالقمل حتى يقتله القمل وكان ذلك أحب إليهم من العطاء". ورواه الحاكم في المستدرك عن عطاء بن يسار عن أبي سعيد الخدري رضي الله تعالى عنه قال : " دخلت على النبي وهو محموم فوضعت يدي من فوق القطيفة فوجدت حرارة الحمى فقلت : ما أشد حماك يا رسول الله ! قال : إنا كذلك معشر الأنبياء يضاعف علينا الوجع ليضاعف لنا الأجر قال : فقلت : يا رسول الله أي الناس أشد بلاء؟ قال : الأنبياء قلت : ثم من؟ قال : ثم الصالحون إن كان الرجل ليبتلى بالفقر حتى ما يجد إلا العباء فيحويها ويلبسها وإن كان أحدهم ليبتلى بالقمل حتى يقتله القمل وكان ذلك أحب إليهم من العطاء إليكم" هذا حديث صحيح على شرط مسلم ولم يخرجاه.(س). قال الإمام القشيري : ليس كل أحد أهلاً للبلاء إذ البلاء للأولياء، وأما الأجانب فيتجاوز عنهم ويخلي سبيلهم، وروي أنه أراد أن يتزوج بامرأة فقيل له : إنها لم تمرض فأعرض عنها، وحكي أن عمار بن ياسر تزوج امرأة لم تمرض فطلقها. (ج) واعلم أن عروض هذه المشاق للأنبياء والأولياء يناسب وظيفتهم التي كلفهم الله تعالى بها، وقاموا هم بحقها، فإن هذه الأمور لا بد أن تلاقي المناكدة من عامة الناس. مما يترتب على الصبر على ذلك عظيم الثواب وهكذا شأن كل من تصدى للقيام بهذه الوظيفة، فإنها عظيمة الخطر بالغة التأثير وما كان هذا شأنه فلا بد أن يوجد من يعارضه يقاوم الداعي إليه ، فتنبه (س).
(1) Ibn Abi al-Dunya narrated in the Book of Sickness and Expiation from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: 'I entered upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and he was feverish. I placed my hand over the quilt and felt the heat of the fever. I said: O Messenger of Allah, how severe is your fever! He said: Indeed, we, the company of prophets, are multiplied in pain so that the reward is multiplied for us. I said: O Messenger of Allah, which people are most severely tried? He said: The prophets. I said: Then who? He said: Then the righteous. Indeed, one of them is tried with poverty until he finds nothing but a cloak, so he dons it and wears it. And indeed, one of them is tried with lice until the lice kill him, and that is more beloved to them than gifts.' And al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak from 'Ata' ibn Yasar from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: 'I entered upon the Prophet and he was feverish...' [similar]. This hadith is authentic according to the condition of Muslim, but they did not record it. Imam al-Qushayri said: Not everyone is worthy of trial, for trial is for the saints (awliya). As for strangers, they are overlooked and left alone. It is narrated that he wanted to marry a woman and it was said to him: She has never been ill, so he turned away from her. And it is related that 'Ammar ibn Yasir married a woman who had never been ill and divorced her. And know that the occurrence of these hardships upon prophets and saints is befitting their function which Allah Most High entrusted them with, and they fulfilled its right. For these matters must face opposition from the general public. What follows from patience upon that is great reward. Such is the case of everyone who undertakes this function, for it is great in import and far-reaching in effect. And since this is its nature, there must be someone who opposes and resists the caller to it. So be mindful.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a citation and commentary on hadith reports about the severity of trials upon prophets and the righteous. The author first presents two versions of a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, one narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya and the other by al-Hakim. In both, the Prophet is suffering from fever, and when asked about it, he explains that prophets have their pain multiplied for multiplied reward. When asked who is most severely tried, he answers: 'The prophets, then the righteous,' and describes the extreme poverty and affliction (lice) that the righteous endure, which they prefer over worldly gifts. The author notes that the hadith is authentic according to Muslim's criteria but not recorded by Bukhari and Muslim. Then he quotes Imam al-Qushayri, who states that not everyone is fit for trial; trial is for the awliya (saints), while others are left alone. An anecdote is given: someone wanted to marry a woman who had never been ill and turned away from her upon learning that. Similarly, 'Ammar ibn Yasir divorced a woman who had never been ill. The author then adds a general observation: these hardships are appropriate for the function of prophets and saints, because their mission inevitably encounters opposition and resistance from people. The reward for patience is great, and anyone who undertakes this function must expect such trials. The passage ends with a call to be mindful of this reality.

الصالحون
الأولياء
الثواب
الوظيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That severe trials indicate God's displeasure or punishment.
Correction: The hadith shows that trials are a sign of closeness and multiplied reward for prophets and saints.

Checkpoint

A) The righteous
B) The prophets
C) The common believers
D) The disbelievers

Key Takeaway
Trials for prophets and saints are a sign of divine favor and an inevitable part of their sacred function, leading to immense reward through patience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The hadith says the righteous love trials more than gifts. Honestly ask yourself: do you love ease more than the opportunity to earn reward through patience? What would it take for you to genuinely welcome trials as a blessing?

Consolation and the Lowly Status of the World
Sanusi explains that prophets' hardships console believers and show the world's low worth before Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophets' hardships console believers and reveal the world's lowly status in Allah's sight.

Core Idea
The prophets' trials show the world is worthless; true honor lies in faith.

This passage from Sanusi draws a profound lesson from the lives of the prophets. By reflecting on the severe hardships faced by the most honorable of creation, we learn both to find solace in our own trials and to recognize that worldly success is not a measure of divine favor. Let's explore these two interconnected points.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Tasalli (Consolation)
Read the definition: patience and comfort in losing worldly pleasures, because the prophets endured hardships. If they suffered, ordinary people are more deserving, so they can take solace in the prophets.
Notice the term 'التصبر' emphasizes patience.
2
Recognize the lowly status of the world
The passage argues that observing the prophets' trials proves the world is worthless to Allah. If it had value, Allah would have given it to the noble and withheld from the wicked.
This refutes the idea that worldly success indicates divine favor.
3
Connect to the broader lesson
Apply this understanding: when facing hardships, remember the prophets and know that the world is not a place of reward but of trial. True honor is in faith, not material gain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التسلي : أي التصبر ووجود الراحة واللذة عن الدنيا عند فقدها لأجل كونهم أكرم الخلق على الله أصابتهم الشدائد وكان من دونهم من باقي البشر أحرى. فإذا أصابت باقي البشر تسلى هؤلاء بالرسل عن الدنيا. التنبيه لخسة قدر الدنيا عند الله ، فإن العاقل إذا نظر في ما واجهه الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام في هذه الدنيا تبين لهم قطعاً أن الدنيا خسيسة القدر عند الله إذ لو كان لها بال (1) لأعطاها السادة الكرام ومنعها الفجار اللثام ) ، وإن الله لم يرض الدنيا دار جزاء لأوليائه بسبب اعتبار أحوال الرسل من الضيق والشدائد.
Al-Tasalli: i.e., patience and finding comfort and pleasure away from the world when it is lost, because they are the most honorable of creation to Allah. Hardships afflicted them, while those below them from the rest of humanity are more deserving. So when hardships afflict the rest of humanity, these people take solace in the messengers concerning the world. The alerting to the lowly status of the world with Allah: for the intelligent person, when he looks at what the prophets (peace and blessings upon them) faced in this world, it becomes absolutely clear to them that the world is of lowly status with Allah. For if it had any weight (1), He would have given it to the noble masters and withheld it from the wicked. And Allah did not approve the world as an abode of recompense for His saints, due to consideration of the conditions of the messengers from hardship and severity.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage consists of two related points: 'al-Tasalli' (consolation) and 'al-Tanbih li-khissati qadr al-dunya' (alerting to the lowly status of the world). First, al-Tasalli is defined as patience and finding comfort in the loss of worldly pleasures, because the prophets—the most honorable of creation—endured severe hardships. If even they suffered, then ordinary humans, who are less than them, are even more deserving of such trials. When ordinary people face hardships, they can console themselves by looking at the prophets and finding solace in them regarding worldly matters. Second, the passage alerts us to the lowly status of the world in Allah's sight. A wise person, upon observing what the prophets encountered—hardship, poverty, illness—will conclude that the world is worthless to Allah. If it had any value, Allah would have given it to the noble prophets and saints and withheld it from the wicked. Instead, Allah did not make the world a place of reward for His saints; rather, the world is a place of trial, as seen in the conditions of the messengers.

التصبر
خسة قدر الدنيا
السادة الكرام
الفجار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Worldly success indicates divine favor; the wealthy and powerful are blessed.
Correction: The passage shows that the prophets, the most honored, were not given worldly wealth. If the world had value, Allah would have given it to them. Thus, worldly success is not a sign of favor.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the world is of lowly status with Allah?
A) Because it is temporary
B) Because Allah did not give it to the prophets and gave it to the wicked
C) Because it is full of sin
D) Because it distracts from worship

Key Takeaway
The world's true value is measured not by material wealth but by faith and patience, as exemplified by the prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you truly believed the world is worthless in Allah's sight, what would you change about your priorities today? Are you willing to live as if the only value is in faith and patience?
?
The prophets—the best of creation—suffered most. Does that not make you reconsider your own complaints? How can you train yourself to see each trial as a potential mark of honor rather than a punishment?

The Prophet's Asceticism and Its Implications
Sanusi declares the Prophet’s asceticism and forbids calling him poor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's lack of worldly wealth was voluntary asceticism, not poverty, and why calling him poor is a grave error.

Core Idea
The Prophet’s poverty was chosen; calling him poor is a capital offense.

In this note, Sanusi clarifies a point of immense respect for the Prophet (peace be upon him) and all prophets. He emphasizes that their detachment from worldly goods was a deliberate choice, not a sign of poverty. This distinction is so critical that Sanusi states that calling them poor warrants capital punishment. Let us examine the passage to grasp the reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage attentively
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the strong opening assertion and the severe ruling that follows.
Pay attention to the phrase 'فلا يقال إنه فقير' – the prohibition is absolute.
2
Identify the key claim and evidence
Sanusi first states that the Prophet was ascetic, giving the example of mountains offering gold. Then he issues the ruling. Two hadiths are provided as evidence for the low value of the world.
The ruling is justified by the fact that the Prophet’s lack of wealth was due to asceticism, not need.
3
Understand the severity of the ruling
The passage declares that whoever calls the Prophet poor should be killed. This shows the extreme importance of maintaining proper respect.
This ruling applies to all prophets, as mentioned.
4
Reflect on the hadiths
The two hadiths demonstrate that the world is insignificant to Allah. This underscores why prophets would choose to abandon it.
The second hadith includes the addition 'and count yourself among the people of the graves.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملاحظة : اعلم أن النبي ترك الدنيا ) زاهداً فيها وكذلك الأنبياء، وقد راودته : الجبال أن تكون ذهباً فأبى. فلا يقال إنه الا الله فقير ولا مسكين ومن قال ذلك يقتل. وكذلك الأنبياء كلهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام. (۱) قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : "لو كانت الدنيا تزن عند الله جناح بعوضة ما سقى الكافر منها جرعة ماء". وقال صلى الله عليه وسلم خطاباً لابن عمر والمراد ما يعمه وغيره : "كن في الدنيا كأنك غريب أو عابر سبيل". زاد الترمذي" وعد نفسك من أهل القبور" .(ج) والحديث الأول أخرجه ابن ماجه والترمذي وقال حديث حسن صحيح. والثاني أخرجه البخاري وزاد أحمد وابن ماجه والترمذي وعد نفسك من أهل القبور (س)
Note: Know that the Prophet left the world, being ascetic in it, and likewise the prophets. And the mountains tempted him to become gold, but he refused. So it should not be said that he is (except Allah) poor or indigent, and whoever says that should be killed. And likewise all the prophets, peace and blessings upon them. (1) The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If the world weighed with Allah the wing of a mosquito, He would not have given a drink of water to a disbeliever from it.' And he (peace be upon him) said, addressing Ibn 'Umar, intending what encompasses him and others: 'Be in the world as if you were a stranger or a wayfarer.' At-Tirmidhi added: 'And count yourself among the people of the graves.' The first hadith is narrated by Ibn Majah and at-Tirmidhi, and he said: a good and authentic hadith. The second is narrated by al-Bukhari, and Ahmad, Ibn Majah, and at-Tirmidhi added: 'And count yourself among the people of the graves.'
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a note (mulahaza) on the asceticism of the Prophet and all prophets. It begins by stating that the Prophet abandoned the world willingly as an ascetic, and so did all prophets. An example is given: the mountains offered to turn into gold for him, but he refused. The note then issues a severe warning: one should not call the Prophet (or any prophet) 'poor' (faqir) or 'indigent' (miskin). Whoever does so is to be killed. This is because their lack of worldly possessions is not due to poverty but to voluntary renunciation. The passage then cites two hadith to support the lowly value of the world: the first hadith states that if the world were worth a mosquito's wing to Allah, He would not give even a drink of water to a disbeliever. The second hadith advises believers to live as strangers or wayfarers in the world, and to count themselves among the dead. The author also provides the hadith sources and their authenticity grades.

Key Terms
زهد
فقير
مسكين
الدنيا
الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet was poor because he lacked worldly wealth.
Correction: His lack of wealth was a voluntary choice of asceticism, not a state of poverty. Calling him poor denies his deliberate renunciation.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling according to this passage for someone who calls the Prophet 'poor'?
A) They should be admonished
B) They should be killed
C) They should be ignored
D) They should be forgiven

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's lack of worldly possessions was a deliberate act of asceticism, not poverty, and calling him poor is a grave offense meriting capital punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet refused mountains of gold. When you look at your own desire for wealth and comfort, can you honestly say you would refuse such an offer? What does your attachment to worldly things reveal about the state of your heart, and what step will you take today to increase your detachment?
?
If calling the Prophet 'poor' is a capital offense, how carefully do you guard your tongue when speaking about him? Think of any careless joke or remark you've made about the Prophet or his life. Will you repent sincerely and commit to honoring him with your words from now on?
?
The world is so insignificant before Allah that a disbeliever would not get even a sip of water if it had value. Yet you chase its pleasures daily. What specific worldly desire are you holding onto that contradicts the way of the Prophet? What will you sacrifice this week to align yourself more with his ascetic spirit?

The Lowliness of the World and the Prophets' Asceticism
Sanusi explains the low status of the world and the prophets' asceticism as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the prophets' worldly hardships demonstrate the insignificance of this world and why calling the Prophet poor is forbidden.

Core Idea
The world's low worth is proven by the prophets' suffering.

Sanusi offers a profound reminder: the suffering of the prophets in this world is not a sign of their low rank but of the world's low worth. Their voluntary renunciation further elevates their status. This lesson explores that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the two distinct parts: a reminder (تنبيه) and a note (ملاحظة).
The style is direct and emphatic.
2
Understand the proof from prophets' hardship
Sanusi argues that if the world had value, Allah would have given it to the prophets. Instead, they faced hardship. Reflect on why this is a logical proof.
3
Grasp the asceticism of the Prophet
The Prophet renounced wealth, even refusing mountains of gold. This shows his high station, not poverty. Note the severe warning against calling him poor.
This connects to respect for prophetic dignity.
4
Reflect on the theological message
Consider how this teaching shapes a Muslim's attitude toward worldly wealth and status. The prophets' example guides us to value the Hereafter over the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التنبيه لخسة قدر الدنيا عند الله ، فإن العاقل إذا نظر في ما واجهه الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام في هذه الدنيا تبين لهم قطعاً أن الدنيا خسيسة القدر عند الله إذ لو كان لها بال (1) لأعطاها السادة الكرام ومنعها الفجار اللثام ) ، وإن الله لم يرض الدنيا دار جزاء لأوليائه بسبب اعتبار أحوال الرسل من الضيق والشدائد. ملاحظة : اعلم أن النبي ترك الدنيا ) زاهداً فيها وكذلك الأنبياء، وقد راودته : الجبال أن تكون ذهباً فأبى. فلا يقال إنه الا الله فقير ولا مسكين ومن قال ذلك يقتل. وكذلك الأنبياء كلهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام.
A reminder of the lowly worth of the world with Allah. For the intelligent person, when he considers what the prophets (peace and blessings be upon them) faced in this world, it becomes absolutely clear to them that the world is of lowly worth with Allah, because if it had any value (1) He would have given it to the noble masters and denied it to the wicked reprobates. And Allah was not pleased to make the world a recompense for His allies, due to consideration of the states of the messengers of hardship and severity. Note: Know that the Prophet left the world, renouncing it, and likewise the prophets. The mountains offered to become gold for him, but he refused. So it should not be said that he is poor or destitute, and whoever says that is to be killed. And likewise all the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage consists of two points. First, a reminder (تنبيه) about the lowly status of the world in Allah's sight. The proof is the observation of what the prophets endured in this world: hardships and difficulties. If the world had any value with Allah, He would have given its comforts to the noble prophets and withheld them from the wicked. Instead, the prophets suffered. Second, a note (ملاحظة) affirming the Prophet's asceticism: he renounced the world, refusing offers of wealth (mountains of gold). It also warns against calling the Prophet poor or destitute, as such a statement indicates disrespect and is punishable by death. The passage emphasizes that the prophets' worldly hardship is a sign of the world's insignificance and their high rank.

Misconception: Some think the Prophet's lack of wealth indicates deficiency or that he was poor out of need.
Correction: The passage clarifies that his poverty was voluntary asceticism; he refused wealth, so calling him poor is disrespectful and prohibited.

What the Second Shahada Entails: Belief in All Prophets
Sanusi explains the entailments of the second shahada regarding belief in all prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the second shahada ('Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah') entails affirming all prophets, their infallibility, the obligation to revere them, and the legal consequences of belittling any prophet.

Core Idea
Believing in Muhammad means believing in all prophets—honoring them is obligatory, belittling them is apostasy.

The second part of the shahada is not just about Muhammad; it extends to all prophets. This passage from Sanusi's text explains the full implications, from affirming their existence and rank to the severe punishment for disrespect. Let's explore what this declaration truly requires.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice how the second shahada is unpacked into multiple obligations.
2
Identify the entailments
List the key points: affirming all prophets, their honored rank, infallibility, the first and last prophets, and the duty to revere them.
The passage also includes the ruling on belittling.
3
Focus on the legal ruling
Pay attention to the punishment for belittling a prophet: execution if unrepentant, flogging upon repentance according to Malikis.
This shows the seriousness of reverence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقولنا "محمد رسول الله" يدخل فيه التصديق بجميع الأنبياء ، أي التصديق بوجودهم وأنهم من عباد الله أكرمهم الله تعالى بهذه الرتبة التي لا يصل إليها أحد غيرهم، وأنهم معصومون من الصغائر والكبائر كما تقدم، أولهم سيدنا آدم وآخرهم سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم و به ختم الله النبوة كما قال تعالى ( وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّنَ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٤٠)، عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، ويجب تعظيمهم وتوقيرهم وأن من استخف بأحد منهم قتل كفراً إن لم يتب إجماعاً، وحدا إن تاب عند المالكية.
For our statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' includes affirmation of all the prophets, i.e., affirmation of their existence and that they are among the servants of Allah whom Allah, exalted is He, has honored with this rank which no one else reaches, and that they are infallible (ma'sumun) from minor and major sins as previously mentioned, the first of them is our master Adam and the last of them is our master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and with him Allah sealed prophethood as He said: 'and the seal of the prophets' (Qur'an 33:40), peace and blessings be upon them. And it is obligatory to revere and venerate them, and whoever belittles any one of them is killed as an apostate if he does not repent, by consensus, and flogged if he repents according to the Malikis.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of what is entailed by the second shahada, 'Muhammad Rasul Allah.' It states that this statement includes belief in all prophets: acknowledging their existence, that Allah honored them with a unique rank, and that they are infallible (ma'sum) from both minor and major sins. It then specifies that the first prophet is Adam and the last is Muhammad, citing Qur'an 33:40 to prove the seal of prophethood. The passage further imposes the obligation to revere and venerate all prophets, and prescribes severe punishment for those who belittle any prophet: execution for apostasy if no repentance, and flogging upon repentance according to the Maliki school.

Correction: Believing in Muhammad implies believing in all prophets, as explained in this passage.

Key Takeaway
The shahada 'Muhammad Rasul Allah' entails affirming all prophets, their infallibility, revering them, and imposes severe punishment for belittling any prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage links belief in Muhammad to belief in all previous prophets. Is there any doubt in your heart that denies the prophethood of any prophet? If so, are you willing to repent and fully affirm your shahada? What step will you take to remove that doubt?
